From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Fri Dec  2 16:32:57 2005
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy)
Date: Fri Dec  2 17:23:52 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] SATA hdd -linux installation -reg
In-Reply-To: <20051202092835.77374.qmail@web8511.mail.in.yahoo.com>
References: <20051202092835.77374.qmail@web8511.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <439029E1.40103@tandbintl.com>

j. manikandan wrote:
>   i tried to install the red hat linux 9.0 . It is showing no harddrives found. 
1. SATA Support is very much available with these distributions. You can 
try one of these.
SUSE Linux 9.3 and later's installation kernel, Fedora Core 3 and 
later's, CentOS 4.1 and later's, Red Hat Enterprise Linux 4 and later, 
Gentoo Linux 2004.3 and later's, Knoppix 3.7 and later's, Debian 
3.1/sarge and later's (especially when started with the "bf2.6 boot 
flavour" boot image), Slackware 10.2 w/test26.s boot option, Xandros 
Desktop OS 3.0 and later's, Ubuntu (or Kubuntu) Linux 5.04 "hoary 
hedgehog" and later's, Vector Linux 5.1 and later's, Libranet 3.0 and 
later's, MEPIS Linux 3.3.1 and later's, Kanotix 2005-03 and later's, 
Linspire 5.0 and later's, PCLinux OS preview .81 and later's, 
ArkLinux's, and Mandriva Linux 2005 (Courtesy: 
http://linuxmafia.com/faq/Hardware/sata.html)

2.If you are keen on Redhat 9, Another option is change the IDE mode as 
"Legacy" in your bios. Now Red hat 9.0 will get installed. Its default 
kernel is 2.4.20 (this version does not have SATA support). Download the 
kernel source 2.4.27 or later (which has SATA support) - build and 
install this kernel. Before rebooting change back the IDE mode as SATA 
in your bios. (Hope your motherboard bios has SATA support). Now your 
hdd will be in SATA way.

-- 
Regards,

T.KaruppuSwamy,
T & B International Pvt. Ltd.
Team Leader
(Embedded OS and Microcontrollers)

There was an occasion for me to quote the poem by Tagore on an issue
touching schools at:
http://mm.gnu.org.in/pipermail/fsf-friends/2004-September/002281.html

The thing that has changed since then is that Linus and his friends have
started demanding license fees for using the alleged "linux" trademark.
Those activities are leashed out from www.linuxmark.org   "Linux" is both
the name of a kernel released under the GPL and also the name by which GNU
operating system has been called when run with the said kernel.  "Linux" is
a generic name and distributors and service providers are free to use it as
part of their names, and it has been freely used by many as such for many
years. Though the claim that the word "linux" is a trademark is untenable,
these activities are a big blow to the spirit of of free software. It is
ridiculous to hold the idea that "linux" is "free" - as long its so called
"owner" demands a "fee" for merely using "linux" as part of product names or
labels.   There are many ways to make $money with free software, but this is
not one of them.  Thousands of others have contributed to the development of
the "linux" kernel, and no single person can hold it to ransom.  In this
situation, the OT tag used by Mohammed Riyaz is correct so far as this list
is concerned :(

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Fri Dec  2 23:27:32 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Dec  3 12:58:00 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Hathway internet working wierdly :)
In-Reply-To: <BAY110-F2FC1860555DEE626B13309B4F0@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <20051203072732.72915.qmail@web50214.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi,

--- Aanjhan R <aanjhan7@hotmail.com> wrote:
> When I reboot my notebook, the network doesnt get up
> automatically. 

Because your settings are not persistent.

> I would 
> have to go to yast and reconfigure. Also after
> configuring with yast the gw  
> does not get setup properly so i hve to manually add
> the gw. 

A simple thing to do would be to add your
configuration commands like:

ifconfig eth0 <ip>
route add default gw <ip> 

to any of your startup scripts in /etc/init.d so
everytime on boot, it gets configured.

Subject: [Ilugc] Ubuntu 5.10 installation with MDK 10.1
Message-ID: <20051204070234.28830.qmail@web54508.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi
 
My system is having MDK 10.1 and Windows XP multibooting with Grub (installed in mbr). 
It is working fine. The System config is Intel PIII 937MHz, 815E MB, 256 MB RAM, 40 GB 
HDD.
 
Now I would like to empty the existing 10 GB FAT32 partition and install ubuntu 5.10 
there. Is it OK if I follow the following the steps.
 
1. Selecting the (E: FAT32) for the installation of Ubuntu and show the MDK swap  
partition for swap (Hope ubuntu and MDK can share the same swap space)
2. Finishing the installation without installing Grub
3. Rebooting the system and editing the menu.lst file with appropirate entries to boot 
into Ubuntu.
 
I know the following lines needs to be modified and added in menu.lst file.

title linux (ubuntu)
kernel (hd0,2)/boot/vmlinuz root=/dev/hda3 acpi=ht resume=/dev/hda7 vga=791
initrd (hd0,2)/boot/initrd.img
 
But confused. Will someone in the group check and suggest me the exact changes which I 
have to make in the lines below? I have appended the existing etc/fstab and meun.lst 
listings to verify.

Thanks.
 
R.Dhanagopal
 
 
HDD is partitioned as below:
 C: 10 GB NTFS Where XP is installed
 D: 10 GB FAT 32 contains data
 E: 10 GB FAT 32 contains data (like to install Ubuntu 5.10 by deleting existing data)
 F: Rest  EXT3 and Swap contains MDK 10.1
 
My fstab entries
 
# This file is edited by fstab-sync - see 'man fstab-sync' for details
 
/dev/hda3 / ext3 defaults 1 1
/dev/hdc /mnt/cdrom auto umask=0,user,iocharset=iso8859-
 
1,codepage=850,noauto,ro,exec,users 0 0
/dev/hdd /mnt/cdrom2 iso9660 user,iocharset=iso8859-1,noauto,ro,exec 0 0
none /mnt/floppy supermount dev=/dev/fd0,fs=ext2:vfat,--,umask=0,iocharset=iso8859-
 
1,sync,codepage=850 0 0
/dev/hda1 /mnt/nt ntfs umask=0,iocharset=iso8859-1,nls=iso8859-1,ro 0 0
/dev/hda6 /mnt/win_e vfat umask=0,iocharset=iso8859-1,codepage=850 0 0
/dev/hda5 /mnt/windows vfat umask=0,iocharset=iso8859-1,codepage=850 0 0
none /proc proc defaults 0 0
/dev/hda7 swap swap defaults 0 0
 
 
 
My menu.lst file 
 
timeout 10
color black/cyan yellow/cyan
default 2
 
title linux
kernel (hd0,2)/boot/vmlinuz root=/dev/hda3 acpi=ht resume=/dev/hda7 vga=791
initrd (hd0,2)/boot/initrd.img
 
title failsafe
kernel (hd0,2)/boot/vmlinuz root=/dev/hda3 failsafe acpi=ht resume=/dev/hda7 
 
devfs=nomount
initrd (hd0,2)/boot/initrd.img
 
title windows
root (hd0,0)
chainloader +1

Hi,

> I get only a terminal window and
> nothing else.

Hmm, this usually happens, if the init script for the desktop
envt/window manager fails or something, it is the failsafe default, so
I guess the upgrade to latest kde broke the init scripts for KDE. The
init scripts are in different places in different distributions, but
common places include /etc/gdm, /etc/X11, etc.

Also, check the .xsession-errors file in ur home directory for clues.

Well, thats my guess anyway! :)

HTH.

On 04/12/05, T.R.Shashwath <trshash84@gmail.com> wrote:
> Best use some distro with a 2.6 kernel. Using RH 9 is like using Windows 95,
> considering the developments we've had since then...

What a comparison. RH 9 is still good enough for a lot of people who
run webservers and such on that platform.

In fact, the OP's SATA disk can be made to work on RH9 by someone with
a bit of knowledge and patience - all it probably needs is to build a
2.6 series kernel and a few userland stuff - modutils etc. on RH 9.
Quite likely everything that is needed is already available on
http://www.fedoralegacy.org. Even more likely that the RHEL2.1 kernel
source RPMs (which includes SATA support) can be rebuilt on RH9.

Binand

From rajagopal.n at gmail.com  Mon Dec  5 08:40:51 2005
From: rajagopal.n at gmail.com (Rajagopal Natarajan)
Date: Mon Dec  5 08:41:00 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] IE Bug Lets Hackers Phish With Google Desktop
Message-ID: <e0900f3e0512041910o36ab5a97u59ecc6f5df51a6b3@mail.gmail.com>

http://www.pcworld.com/news/article/0,aid,123826,00.asp

 IE Bug Lets Hackers Phish With Google Desktop
Hacker could scan your hard drive and steal sensitive info.

 Robert McMillan, IDG News Service
Friday, December 02, 2005

A bug in Microsoft's Internet Explorer browser gives phishers a way to scan
the hard drives of Google Desktop users, according to an Israeli hacker.
Because of a flaw in the way IE processes Web pages, a malicious Web site
could use the attack to steal sensitive information like credit card numbers
or passwords from the hard drives of its visitors.

"Google Desktop
<http://www.pcworld.com/reviews/article/0,aid,122374,00.asp>users who
use IE are currently completely exposed," wrote hacker Matan
Gillon in an e-mail interview. "An experienced attacker can covertly harvest
their hard drives for sensitive information such as passwords and credit
card numbers. Since Google also indexes e-mails which can be read in the Web
interface itself, it's also possible to access them using this attack."
The Details

Gillon has posted an extensive description of how such an attack would work,
along with a proof of concept exploit, on his
blog<http://www.hacker.co.il/security/ie/css_import.html>
.

The IE bug concerns the way Microsoft's browser processes Web page layout
information using the CSS (Cascading Style Sheets) format. The CSS format is
widely used to give Web sites a consistent look and feel, but attackers can
take advantage of the way that IE processes CSS to get Google Desktop to
reveal sensitive information.

Hackers would first need to trick users into visiting a malicious Web site
for the attack to be successful, Gillon says. The attack works with IE 6 and
Google Desktop version 2, and may also work on other versions of Microsoft's
browser, but not on non-Microsoft browsers like Firefox or Opera, he adds.
Turn Off JavaScript

Users can nullify the attack by turning off JavaScript in their browsers,
Gillon says. This can be done by disabling "Active scripting" in IE's
Internet Options menu.
JavaScript<http://www.pcworld.com/news/article/0,aid,123764,00.asp>is
a popular scripting language used by Web developers to make their
sites
more dynamic.

Users need to be particularly wary of the Web sites they visit these days,
because of another unpatched IE vulnerability that could be used to take
over a user's PC. Hackers posted sample code that exploited this problem
over a week ago, and Microsoft said that hackers are already using the code
in attacks. As with the new CSS problem, users must first be tricked into
visiting a malicious Web site for this IE bug to be exploited.

Some security experts believe that Microsoft is in the process of rushing
out a patch to fix this problem before these attacks become more widespread.
These attacks can also be avoided by disabling JavaScript in IE, or by using
an alternative browser.

Microsoft executives were unavailable to comment on the CSS bug, but a
spokeswoman for the company's public relations agency said the issue is
being investigated. Microsoft is not aware of any attacks resulting from the
hole, she said.

Dhanagopal Rengasamy wrote:
> 2. Finishing the installation without installing Grub
> 3. Rebooting the system and editing the menu.lst file with appropirate entries to boot 
> into Ubuntu.
>  
It is ***better to install grub on Ubuntu root partition*** (/dev/hda3 
in your case). After reboot, you can boot to MDK. Take the entry of 
Ubuntu in menu.lst of ubuntu partition and append it with the menu.lst 
of MDK. It is better to take the kernel argument set by distributor, 
since they customize the kernel.

it should give you a list of alternatives... select the appropriate

Had a quick looksee in the linuxmark.org website. From what I gather,
ILUGC or anyone else  (even commercial entities earning less than
USD50K per annum) do not have to pay anything. They only have to
attribute the linux trademark to the relevant owners.

Am sure it cost money to defend the status quo in Australia. Who pays
for it? I think linuxmark.org is a reasonable solution to this problem
- if you make a lot of money then pay us an amt so we can use it to
ward off threats.

Revisiting the discussion on BLUG being hijacked and controls in place
for chennailug, what stops someone from registering chennailug as a
society (without chennailug.org knowing it?). Even if it will be
untenable in a court and the society can be declared illegal, who will
pay for the costs to get such a judgement?

On 12/4/05, Binand Sethumadhavan <binand@gmail.com> wrote:
> What a comparison. RH 9 is still good enough for a lot of people who
> run webservers and such on that platform.

Which is probably not what most desktop/end users want... ;-)

> In fact, the OP's SATA disk can be made to work on RH9 by someone with
> a bit of knowledge and patience - all it probably needs is to build a
> 2.6 series kernel and a few userland stuff - modutils etc. on RH 9.
> Quite likely everything that is needed is already available on
> http://www.fedoralegacy.org. Even more likely that the RHEL2.1 kernel
> source RPMs (which includes SATA support) can be rebuilt on RH9.

Lot more painful to do that and keep such a system upto date, than
just installing a distro built around 2.6, I think... Point I'm making
is that if you're not experienced enough to do that much maintainence,
RH9 is not worth the trouble...
--
Shash

From raja.mallik at moschip.com  Mon Dec  5 10:26:47 2005
From: raja.mallik at moschip.com (Raja Mallik)
Date: Mon Dec  5 15:56:49 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Upgrading to SATA !!
In-Reply-To: <a8427db00512050039v7c413e1ax2cb0fc13ac257ca4@mail.gmail.com>
References: <20051202092835.77374.qmail@web8511.mail.in.yahoo.com>
	<200512042046.21566.trshash84@gmail.com>
	<d2a92d610512040934r2d6d84b2i@mail.gmail.com>
	<a8427db00512050039v7c413e1ax2cb0fc13ac257ca4@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <1133777855.22494.4377.camel@mazda>


Hi all, 

I have made a PCI base serail ATA drive work with linux-2.6 series!
Just check if that helps and yes 2.6 kernel is best to make sata work
instead of 2.4 series comes with redhat 9!


FY!
---------------------------------------------------------------------

This PCI Serai ATA host controller card support for linux is available
in most of the latest kernel release. 


Step 1) Make a kernel image that support PCI Serial ATA controller.
Vendor : Silicon Image


Configure a fresh linux-2.6.12.tar.gz kernel and adding this few options
should enable the should make the kernel recognize the IDE controller
card when we plug into PCI slot of your standalone PC or other board.


#tar -xvzf linux-2.6.12.tar.gz

#cdlinux-2.6.12

#make menuconfig


Device Drivers --->

SCSI device support --->

<M> SCSI device support

[*] legacy /proc/scsi/ support

--- SCSI support type (disk, tape, CD-ROM)

<M> SCSI disk support

<M> SCSI tape support

<M> SCSI OnStream SC-x0 tape support

<M> SCSI CDROM support

[*] Enable vendor-specific extensions (for SCSI CDROM)

<M> SCSI generic support

[*] Verbose SCSI error reporting (kernel size +=12K)

[*] SCSI logging facility

SCSI Transport Attributes --->

SCSI low-level drivers --->

[*] Serial ATA (SATA) support

<M> AHCI SATA support

<M> ServerWorks Frodo / Apple K2 SATA support

<M> Intel PIIX/ICH SATA suppor

<M> Promise SATA SX4 support

<M> Silicon Image SATA support 

File systems---->

<*> Second extended fs support 

[*] Ext2 extended attributes 

[*] Ext2 POSIX Access Control Lists 

[*] Ext2 Security Labels 

<M> Ext3 journalling file system support 

[*] Ext3 extended attributes 

[*] Ext3 POSIX Access Control Lists 

[ ] Ext3 Security Labels 

[*] JBD (ext3) debugging support

DOS/FAT/NT Filesystems --->

M> MSDOS fs support 

<M> VFAT (Windows-95) fs support 

(437) Default codepage for FAT 

(iso8859-1) Default iocharset for FAT 

<M> NTFS file system support




Save the configuration and build the image as:

#make bzImage

#make modules;

#make modules_install

#make install

#lilo


Step 2) Shutdown the machine and make sure power is OFF.


Step 3) Installing the Serial ATA controller card into your PC.


a) Align the Serai ATA controller card w.r.tPCI slot and insert it.

b) connect to the sata connector of Serial ATA controller cable to the
SATA hard disk.

c) connect the power supply from PC ( with SATA pluggins from the Vendor
that can be used with 

default SMPS we have in PC) to the SATA hard disk.


Step 4) Start Power ON to the PC and Boot form the new kernel
image(2.6.12) that 

we have built. Once the PC is booted with new kernel.


Step 5) Driver installations:

#modprobe scsi

#modprobe sd_mod

#modprobe dm_mod

#modprobe sg

#modprobe st

#modprobe ide-scsi

#modprobe libata

#modprobe sata_sil /* This is the main driver for us to have access to
SATA disk


#

#fdisk -l 

This will show the disk partion of your local PC and the external IDE
hard disk drive that we have installed. This is what it shows for my PC:


Disk /dev/hda: 40.0 GB, 40020664320 bytes

255 heads, 63 sectors/track, 4865 cylinders

Units = cylinders of 16065 * 512 = 8225280 bytes


Device Boot Start End Blocks Id System

/dev/hda1 * 1 1276 10249438+ c Win95 FAT32 (LBA)

/dev/hda2 1277 4865 28828642+ f Win95 Ext'd (LBA)

/dev/hda5 1277 2522 10008463+ b Win95 FAT32

/dev/hda6 2523 2535 104391 83 Linux

/dev/hda7 2536 3682 9213246 83 Linux

/dev/hda8 3683 4064 3068383+ 83 Linux

/dev/hda9 4065 4446 3068383+ 83 Linux

/dev/hda10 4447 4697 2016126 83 Linux

/dev/hda11 4698 4763 530113+ 82 Linux swap

/dev/hda12 4764 4814 409626 83 Linux

/dev/hda13 4815 4865 409626 83 Linux


Disk /dev/sda: 251.0 GB, 251000193024 bytes

255 heads, 63 sectors/track, 30515 cylinders

Units = cylinders of 16065 * 512 = 8225280 bytes


Disk /dev/sda doesn't contain a valid partition table

Note: This is a new disk wit no data in any format. Else all the
partition of the disk will show up.




Step 6) Accessing the new STAT hard drive.


#mkdir test

#modprobe ext3

#modporbe ext2

#modprobe msdos

#modprebe ntfs


#mount /dev/sda* test/


So all contains in /dev/sda* are there in test.



Here what minimimal needs to be selected to make Serial ATA controller
work on board: 

Regards
Raja Mallik

Subject: [Ilugc] Year 2038..Again the replica of Y2K ??
In-Reply-To: <20051130133017.44906.qmail@web54302.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20051130133017.44906.qmail@web54302.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <495e45120512051835p2f77eed1ja4221bf077d0f489@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/30/05, Karthik <karthik_cec@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Hi,
>
>   Read the information below, which i got in a mail.
>
>   In unix, is time_t,  type defined from an int data type ?? Will unix based n/w applications crash during 2038? any suggestions??
>
>   **********************************************************
>   The Year 2038 Problem
>       Test it now.   steps...       1. login to yahoo messenger   2. send instant message to anyone - fine its working...   3. now, change ur system date to 19-Jan-2038, 03:14:07 AM or above   4. Confirm weather ur date is changed   5. again send instant message to anyone...   Your YM crahes....   ( while trying these steps close ur applications/IE ..etc ??.  my IE got corruptted and I had to reinstall )     * * * YES ALL NETWORK BASED APPLICATION WILL NOT WORK NOW * * *   Why.....
>
>   What is it?   Starting at GMT 03:14:07, Tuesday, January 19, 2038, It is expected to see lots of systems around the world breaking Magnificently. In short, many of the dire predictions for the year 2000 are much more likely to actually occur in the year 2038! Consider the year 2000 just a dry run. In case you think we can sit on this issue for another 30 years before addressing it, consider that reports of temporal echoes of the 2038 problem are already starting to appear in future date calculations for mortgages and vital statistics!   In the first month of the year 2038 C.E. many computers will encounter a date-related bug in their operating systems and/or in the applications they run. This can result in incorrect and wildly inaccurate dates being reported by the operating system and/or applications. The effect of this bug is hard to predict, because many applications are not prepared for the resulting "skip" in reported time anywhere from 1901 to a "broken record" repeat
>   of the
>  reported time at the second the bug occurs. Also, may make some small adjustment to the actual time the bug expresses itself. This bug to cause serious problems on many platforms, especially Unix and Unix-like platforms, because these systems will "run out of time".
>
>   What causes it?   Time_t is a data type used by C and C++ programs to represent dates and times internally. (Windows programmers out there might also recognize it as the basis for the CTime and CTimeSpan classes in MFC.)   time_t is actually just an integer (a whole number), that counts the number of seconds since January 1, 1970 at 12:00 AM Greenwich Mean Time. A time_t value of 0 would be 12:00:00 AM (exactly midnight) 1-Jan-1970, a time_t value of 1   would be 12:00:01 AM  (one second after midnight) 1-Jan-1970, etc..   some example times and their exact time_t representations:   Date & time     time_t representation   1-Jan-1970,     12:00:00 AM GMT 0   1-Jan-1970,     12:01:00 AM GMT 60   1-Jan-1970,     01:00:00 AM GMT 3 600   2-Jan-1970,     12:00:00 AM GMT 86 400   1-Jan-1971,     12:00:00 AM GMT 31 536 000   1-Jan-1972,     12:00:00 AM GMT 63 072 000   1-Jan-2038,     12:00:00 AM GMT 2 145 916 800   19-Jan-2038,    03:14:07 AM GMT 2 147 483 647   By the year 2038,
>  the
>  time_t representation for the current time will be over 2 140 000 000.   And that's the problem. A modern 32-bit computer stores a "signed integer" data type, such as time_t, in 32 bits. The First of these bits is used for the positive/negative sign of the integer, while the remaining 31 bits are used to store the number itself.   The highest number these 31 data bits can store works out to exactly 2147 483 647.   A time_t value of this exact number, 2 147 483 647, represents January 19,2038, at 7 seconds past 3:14 AM Greenwich Mean Time. So, at 3:14:07 AM GMT on that fateful day, every time_t used in a 32-bit C or C++ program will reach its upper limit.   One second later, on 19-January-2038 at 3:14:08 AM GMT, disaster strikes.   When a signed integer reaches its maximum value and then gets incremented, it wraps around to its lowest possible negative value. This means a 32-bit signed integer, such as a time_t, set to its maximum value of 2 147 483 647 and then incremented b
>  y 1,
>  will become -2 147 483 648.   Note that "-" sign at the beginning of this large number. A time_t value of -2 147 483 648 would represent December 13, 1901 at 8:45:52 PM GMT.   So, if all goes normally, 19-January-2038 will suddenly become 13-December-1901 in every time_t across the globe, and every date calculation based on this figure will go haywire. And it gets worse.
> Most of the support functions that use the time_t data type cannot handle negative time_t values at all. They simply fail and return an error code.
>
             This theory is based on thee fact that most computers
today are 32-bit. But as we are already seeing, computers migrating
towards 64-bit computing. So think of what would be the norm in 2038,
where computers would be 64-bit or higher say 128-bit. Which means
this is not likely to occur even in 2068.

with regards,
ashwin

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Tue Dec  6 08:48:32 2005
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Tue Dec  6 08:48:41 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: time_t date problem in 2038
Message-ID: <1266.61.247.255.57.1133839112.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

> Most of the support functions that use the time_t data type cannot handle
> negative time_t values at all. They simply fail and return an error code.

>This theory is based on thee fact that most computers today are 32-bit.
But >as we are already seeing, computers migrating towards 64-bit
computing. So >think of what would be the norm in 2038, where computers
would be 64-bit or >higher say 128-bit. Which means this is not likely to
occur even in 2068.

>with regards,
>ashwin

The move to 64-bit processor will not mitigate the need to make changes in
the date handling functions and at the very least do a full re-compile. A
lot of the date handling functions use OR and AND operations to pack date
values - these will have to be modified.

The problem is that 64-bit processors are normally run in "Compatibility
mode" which essentially means that the processor will treat Integers as
32-bit values rather than the full 64-bit so as not to break applications
which are compiled only with 32-bit support. However, the processor does
support the running of both 64-bit and 32-bit apps at the same time.

This is true for both AMD's and well as Intel's offerings. To understand
this better, please read the documentation for these processors. AMD64 has
two primary modes of operation - the "Long" mode and the "Legacy" mode.
The long mode has two sub-modes - one being the 64-bit mode and the other
being the "Compatibility Mode" which I wrote about.

But yes, the situation is not that dire. A few minor changes in the date
handling code and a full recompile will solve most issues.

Regards,
Prem Kurian Philip
Songbird Technologies

Hi,

AFAIK today's 64-bit processors are designed to support both 32-bit &
64-bit apps. This is because, as you might have already know, 32-bit
is dominant & most apps are designed to  run on 32-bit,hence this
32-bit support. But as we see more & more 64-bit entering mainstream
(which includes home users b'cos they have a large user base & hence
their need to support them). So we would be seeing more codes for
64-bit computing. Hence i think the bug is not likely to surface in
the predicted time.

with regards,
ashwin

prove that it had the name first. If the name is registered by 
ilugc, the other side would have to go to court. I am of the 
opinion that it is better to register. Incidently, hijacking of 
blug took place not because it was registered, but in spite of the 
fact that it was registered. As long as you have active members and 
the society is registered - no one can hijack it. If there are no 
active members, then it is irrelevant whether it is hijacked or 
not. Just my 2 paise.

Date: Tue Dec  6 10:03:05 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Free Software User Groups
Message-ID: <439515BA.90808@gmail.com>

Rick Moen  has written  an excellent and  useful user group  HOWTO at:
http://www.linux.org/docs/ldp/howto/User-Group-HOWTO.html 
<http://www.linux.org/docs/ldp/howto/User-Group-HOWTO.html>

What follows is about how free software user groups could be organised 
locally in Tamil Nadu.  I wrote most of it sometime back, and the only 
thing I could add is, it may be worthwhile to register marks associated 
with the fsug, if that is perceived as important for the sake of 
identity.  Though "Linux" is a generic word, I would suggest organisers 
to choose a name that is more general like "fsug" as part of the name so 
that the scope is as wide as possible to include discussions about 
Linux, GNU, FreeBSD or the others.

There is a proposal to allow Limited Liability Partnerships in India, 
that could function like companies under the ROC, and this may suit some 
but they would have to wait for the law to crystallise. For now:

Typically, we may classify FSUGs into three categories.

#1: FSUG's Structured within an Institution

Many colleges already have an internet presence, and it is very easy
to run web servers, mailing list servers, ftp, wiki, cvs etc with
minimal effort. Free Software tools like the GNU Mailman, Apache Web
Server, Wikimedia, CVS etc could be installed to set up the bare needs
for setting up a FSUG.  It needs only one Admin and a few volunteers
to keep things going.

ILUGC and many of the FSUGs operating from colleges at present follow
this style, and it is the least cumbersome and most beneficial general
purpose model, that works well from within an institutional framework.
 PostgreSQL, NetBSD and others originated from such an environment.

#2: Informal FSUGs maintained by small groups of individuals, ngo's
and other orgs:

The vast majority of FSUGs have virtual existence, using mailing list
facilities offered by Yahoo, Google, Savannah, SourceForge etc.  It
costs nothing to create a FSUG from these sites, and these FSUGs play
a major role in spreading the use of Free Software in pockets where
there no other help is conceivable.  If you are the lone GNU/Linux
user in your locality, you may think of starting a FSUG for your
locality :)

#3:  FSUGs Registered as a Society/Co-operative Society/Non-profit 
Company/Trust

Legal formalities are the hall-mark of these entities, making it
suitable for only dedicated Free Software enthusiasts who will be
required to interact with statutory authorities to maintain and run
the organisation and may also need to take assistance from
professionals like auditors, lawyers and other experts.

Groups interested in building specialised computer programs,
supercomputers, community kiosks, community wiki, specialised fs
distributions or doing other tasks that involve some investment, would
need to orgranise a framework that can service the ends.

It is very difficult to generalise, but the simplest way to legally
organise a FSUG is to register it as a Society, under the Tamil Nadu
Societies Registration Act, 1975.

A very brief introduction to how Societies are created, maintained and
dissolved:

Any society which has for its object the promotion of education,
literature, science, religion, charity, social reform, art, crafts,
cottage industries, athletics, sports (including indoor games),
recreation, public health, social service, cultural activities, the
diffusion of useful knowledge or such other useful objects within the
State Legislative domain *may* be registered under the Tamil Nadu
Societies Registration Act.

Societies with not less than 20 members or whose annual gross income
or expenditure is not less than Rs.10,000/- need to be compulsorily
registered. For the purpose of registration, the society would need to
file its memorandum specifying the name of the society, the objects of
the society, the names, addresses and occupations of the members of
the committee; and the byelaws of the society.  Every registered
Society shall keep a Registered Office, keep a board (also in Tamil :)
outside its RO, maintain a register containing the names, addresses
and occupation of its members (that is open to inspection during
business hours), have a committee of not less than three members to
manage its affairs whose  term is not to be more than three years and
are appointed at a meeting by a resolution of a majority of members,
keep books of accounts audited by an auditor, file prescribed forms
before the Registrar.  Under bye-laws, members may be required to pay
subscriptions.

Atleast one AGM shall be conducted every year after notice to members,
and minutes shall be maintained and filed.

The society may sue and be sued, members guilty of arrears or
embezzelment may be  dealt with as strangers.

Two or more societies may be amalgamated or a society may divide into
two or more with approval of Registrar.

A Society may be wound up, but after satisfaction of all debts and
liabilities, the remainder shall *not* be paid to members of the
society, but shall be given to some other registered society having
the same or similar objects (that can be determined by a special
resolution of the society itself).

FSUGs organised as Registered Societies in India:

1) Pune GNU/Linux Users Group [PLUG}
http://www.cyberindian.com/india/index.php?action=jump&jumpto=2230 
<http://www.cyberindian.com/india/index.php?action=jump&jumpto=2230>
At their "About us" page:

<quote>
Pune GNU/Linux Users Group or PLUG is a voluntary, not-for-profit
organization. registered under the Indian Societies Act, 1860.Our
registration no. is MH/238/2003/Pune. We are also registered as a
Public Trust having registration no. F19273.
</quote>

2) Linux-Delhi.org says that they are in the process of getting
registered as a Society.  Check out their societification page at
http://www.cyberindian.com/india/index.php?action=jump&jumpto=2225 
<http://www.cyberindian.com/india/index.php?action=jump&jumpto=2225>

NASSCOM  (National Association of Software and Service Companies
www.nasscom.org <http://www.nasscom.org> ) is organised as a Society but 
it is yet to become
seriously involved with the free software movement.  When Free
Software becomes more widely recognised and appreciated, NASSCOM would
necessarily get transformed and may become a nodal point for Free
Software User Groups.

Non-profit Companies and Co-operative societies are even more formal,
and discussing them would make this post much more longer ;)  Free
Software Foundation of India ( www.gnu.org.in <http://www.gnu.org.in> ) 
is registered as a
non-profit company under the Companies Act, with office at Trivandrum.

In Tamil Nadu, the co-operative movement has been successful, and it
may be worth trying out this model, say to build supercomputers or  to
subsidise computer based goodies.  One of the largest organisations
has an annual turnover of more than Rs. 80 Crores.  If any group is
seriously interested in dedicating themselves in this line, it could
benefit the masses in very tangible ways.

Unlike the above not-for-profit entities, if groups are looking for
ways of earning private profit from Free Software, they would organise
themselves as consultants, service providers, run proprietary
concerns, form partnerships, pvt/public limited companies,  and other
types of associations with clear objectives to earn profit.
Generally, providing custom services are the main business of
for-profit organisations, but they invariably extend support to
not-for-profit organisations through donations and offer other kinds
of support.

HTH.

Regards,
Ramanraj.

Hello All,

          In the lines of PDX.rb, Seattle.rb and other Ruby Brigades 
(you can call them ruby user groups) I'm proud to announce the Chennai 
Ruby Brigade, in short called Chennai.rb (.rb is also the extension of a 
Ruby file).

          What do we intend to do? Simple. Learn & enjoy Ruby. Currently 
I'm thinking of a monthly meet up where in we can exchange ideas, cool 
ruby snippets, break our heads on continuations and drool at the latest 
Rails feature. Yes, I'm introduced to Ruby through Rails, and it sure is 
a framework worthy of the language.

          We will discuss the idiosyncrasies of _why's writing style (if 
you're a Ruby fan, you should know who 'Why The Lucky Stiff' is), try to 
answer the weekly Ruby Quiz and start zany/silly projects like Sudoku 
solvers. I promise, we will try to be very elitist, and only the coolest 
and the best talks will be allowed. That is, you give a talk at 
Chennai.rb, you better be prepared. Excited? Here's where you subscribe:

http://groups.google.com/group/chennairb

         As an introductory session, I'm thinking of a one-hour talk 
named "Welcome to Rubyland" on Saturday, the 17th of December (I'm no 
Ruby guru, so if somebody has lots of Ruby experience, they're most 
welcome to give the talk). But remember, prepare, prepare, prepare! We 
all have very little time to blow, so let's make it worth the trouble. 
We will try not to conflict with the ILUGC/GLV meeting timings.

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~ 
First ever Chennai.rb meet up:

Date: 17th December, 2005                                         
Venue: Ma Foi Academy
Time:   Exactly at 4pm IST (No, the time is *not* stretchable)

(Having our meets on 1st/3rd/5th Saturdays means we can have the 
excellent F&H coffee - but no snacks though, unless some noble corporate 
soul sponsors it)
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

Welcome All! Let's have further discussions on the chennai.rb list! All 
the luggers who couldn't be bothered about Ruby, sorry for the noise. 
After all, it's an open source language ;-)

You can keep track of our progress here:

http://chennairb.blogspot.com

Cheers & Thanks,
Vamsee.

From bhuvan at ubuntu.com  Tue Dec  6 16:55:06 2005
From: bhuvan at ubuntu.com (Bhuvaneswaran)
Date: Tue Dec  6 16:55:13 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Does Debian supports 2.6 kernel
In-Reply-To: <20051206104448.18217.qmail@web51601.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20051206104448.18217.qmail@web51601.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4dc6c9040512060325g3179a160p4c6a6e8258887d4e@mail.gmail.com>

> Can anyone tell me how to upgrade the Debian Kernel
> from 2.4 to 2.6.8

Are you trying to migrate from woody -> sarge ? Or, wish to upgrade
just your kernel 2.4 -> 2.8 ? If you meant case (1), i recommend you
to configure /etc/apt/source.list and run 'sudo apt-get dist-upgrade'.
If you meant case (2), confirm 2.6.8 is installed by checking
/lib/modules/. If boot loader resides in the same dir, it would have
got updated automatically. If not, you must edit your boot loader conf
file accordingly and re-install your boot loader.
--
Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran

My mistake. Read that as 292 billion years (2^63 seconds/31 million
seconds/year).

the universe puts it at between 10-15 billion years

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Wed Dec  7 07:54:26 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Wed Dec  7 07:49:50 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Free Software User Groups
In-Reply-To: <7bf1bec50512060013p5562a330obf6c45b96e896691@mail.gmail.com>
References: <439515BA.90808@gmail.com>
	<7bf1bec50512060013p5562a330obf6c45b96e896691@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <439647DA.6090500@gmail.com>

Mano wrote:

>Looks like forming a society will entail more administrative work than
>actually discussing open source issues - sucking out the fun in the
>process. Soon politicking will also set in. And am sure there will be
>bribes to be paid to the clerks, registrars etc. 
>
Any campaign involves resources of people, time and money that are 
limited, and organising them efficiently is the only way to achieve 
productivity.  Most legal devices are designed to enable people in 
society to plan their goals orderly, transparently and peacefully.  In 
well run organisations, the admin, though always around and working, 
would probably never be seen or visible (like the kernel).  In badly run 
ones, the admin would be in the center stage and no work would get done 
without glitches.  The balanced approach to organisation in development 
is elaborately narrated by Frederick P. Brooks in "The Mythical 
Man-Month" drawing from his experience as project manager for IBM 
System/360. Lack of access to computers (minimal to supersize) is a 
matter of concern from the times of Charles Babbage to this day.  If 
everything else has failed, in spite of the problems involved, formal 
organisation could help groups to service their wants - particularly if 
higher level orgs do not give priority to needs.

>So my vote is to let
>things be and hope no one will do the unthinkable. After all who gains
>what by hijacking chennailug!!
>  
>
"TwinCLinG" used for long by ilug-hyd could be seen as "hijacked" by the 
gang at http://www.twincling.org/ or as "sharing" and "contribution" by 
ilug-hyd.  Time will tell if such gangs survive or perish ;)

The software itself is free and there is no point in "branding" 
activities.  In fact, the "brand building strategies" do  more harm than 
good as they tend to spoil portability.  The distro naming mania could 
end if people called the distros they use by the name of installer they 
use: yast, synaptic, apt etc.

>regds,
>mano
>--
>All generalizations are false.
>  
>
"Generality is of two kinds; the more comprehensive, and the less 
comprehensive.
  But, particularities abiding in eternal substances are innumerable 
indeed"  - Tarka Samgraha

Message-ID: <a7a9a950512062039t5a519d7au40480489c404f7b6@mail.gmail.com>

I agree with Ramanraj. His analysis is good. The more dominated, a system or
network, the less preferred it would be.

So the best is to allow people to administer themselves, with the exception
of making personal attacks/totally offtopic marketing, etc.

It should be a true initiative of members, by members, for members.

Registering as a society, if a formality for a bank account, needs just 7
persons and a name, with a President, Secretary, Treasurer and bye-laws and
activities list.

It is preferable to have joint cheque signing powers with any 2 office
bearers. It is prefereable to put in the site all transactions, for
transparency and accountability.

Kris Dev.

Hi,

--- indu veni <pj_indras@yahoo.com> wrote:
>    I want to know whether creating a base system

Which is basically a collection of packages. What is
important is only the versions of the individual
packages.

> using
> Debian system and Fedora system is same or any thing
> varies. 

Debian and Fedora are GNU/Linux distributions. A
distro has a package management system and package
installer. 

You may or may not have a package
manager/package-installer in a base system (example,
embedded systems).

Bhuvaneswaran <bhuvan@ubuntu.com> writes:


> I'm trying to watch TV on my gnu/linux box (FC4) from a cable TV
> connection.  I have a external TV tuner card (USB).  I use mythtv. I'd
> like to know what program to use to tune the channels and find the
> channel frequencies.  If anyone has a TV tuner card installed in a
> gnu/linux machine and is able to watch cable channels, i would

I have internal pinnacle TV tuner card and I use xawtv it works

it for channel scan.

Above all google for the information u need.

---------- Forwarded message ----------
From: Augusta Molnar < amolnar@forest-trends.org>
Date: Dec 8, 2005 6:26 AM
Subject: [GKD] Microsoft Donations: Roses with Thorns?
To: gkd@milhouse.edc.org

Dear GKD Members,

I am writing from Oaxaca, Mexico where I am visiting communities in the
highlands. They have been beneficiaries of a very cool project financed in
part by the Gates foundation to install a wireless connection and a set of
computers for the schools. We are working on a network in the Latin America
region for communities for which we use by preference
FireFox as our browser. We suggested they try this browser as Explorer was
causing problems, and discovered to our surprise that the Gates foundation
"gift" comes with tags.

The computer network does not allow any of the users of the donated
computers to install any software not owned by Microsoft, even any open
source software. The network within which the computers reside will not
allow any individual computers to download software to install, ostensibly
to prevent viruses and incompatible software from jeopardizing the Microsoft
system.

These are computers installed for educational purposes in a number of
telecenters in the public libraries in Mexico for all the young students
preparing for a global world. These computers are therefore their only
affordable access to the Internet and to learning about computers and
programs. A significant number of them will leave this town to work at least
part of their life elsewhere in Mexico or in the U.S. Their work and career
opportunities will depend upon their skills and preparedness.

I am reminded of my youth, working in the vicinity of USAID programs which
only purchased American-made cars shipped to remote corners of Asia for
irrigation projects, etc., because the tied money only allowed US bids.
(Ever try to blow up a pneumatic truck tire with a bicycle pump in a small
town in Asia? )

Is this standard Gates foundation policies?????? Is this type of tag
allowed??

Interested to hear from those of you who are more knowledgeable on this
point.


Augusta Molnar
Director, Community and Markets Program
Forest Trends
1050 Potomac Street NW
Washington, D.C. 20007
Phone: 202 298-3006
Fax: 202 298-3014
www.forest-trends.org

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Thu Dec  8 20:51:54 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Thu Dec  8 20:46:30 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Sponsor .^.Calpp
Message-ID: <43984F92.1000500@gmail.com>

The Calpp project is hosted at:
http://gborg.postgresql.org/cgi-bin/cvsweb.cgi/?cvsroot=calpp

Calpp, released under the GNU  GPL, is a framework to store procedures
and execute them  as proceedings.  Recently, I made  a presentation on
"Calpp &  .^.i" at the Tuxedo  05 event of SJCE,  Mysore.  The slides,
that explain the need for good representations and the basic structure
of Calpp are available online at:
http://gborg.postgresql.org/cgi-bin/cvsweb.cgi/calpp/docs/calpp_ai.pdf?cvsroot=calpp

Calpp will soon go online, thanks to the sponsorship by Anand Avati of
ZResearch,  and  the support by Anand  Babu, co-founder of  ZResearch,
specialising in Supercomputers and  Superstorage.  This would be .^.#1
host on the Home Planet :)

I recently applied for a Fellowship from Sarai,and its details are at:
http://gborg.postgresql.org/cgi-bin/cvsweb.cgi/calpp/docs/calpp_proposal_to_sarai_2005_abridged.pdf?cvsroot=calpp

Free Software  and the Internet  together could become a  paradise for
Law.  Calpp Project aims to port  Law to computers.  If Law, .^.i, and
society excite you, welcome aboard!

-Ramanraj K
__

OED says-
sponsor: a person who introduces and supports a proposal for a new law

I think you were using GRUB installed from Fedora Core before installing
the sarge. So you should have your original menu.lst in the /boot/grub
of FC4 partition. The FC4 entries in this file can be compared with the
current menu.lst to find the odd thing out.

no u dont have to reinstall. if u have the ubuntu live cd.. (or any
other live cd for that matter) put in and boot from it. Then open
terminal and change to root user. now run the command
'grub-install /dev/hda' or replace the device name with your boot
drive (/boot) name. and restart :-)

From aanjhan7 at hotmail.com  Sat Dec 10 05:46:29 2005
From: aanjhan7 at hotmail.com (Aanjhan R)
Date: Sat Dec 10 11:16:39 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: recovering ubuntu 5.10 linux (deepak srinivasan)
In-Reply-To: <20051210050650.2DDC31DB263@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <BAY110-F17070BE02FADB3D2B7A5DB9B440@phx.gbl>


Hello Deepak,

This is the solution.

boot: linux rescue

... and press Enter. The installer will ask you a few questions like the 
language you would like to use, the type of keyboard etc. Then, if you have 
linux previously installed on your machine, the installer will automatically 
detect it and mount it in the /mnt/sysimage directory. Once the linux 
partition is mounted, you are dropped into the command shell prompt. The 
next step is to make your newly mounted directory the root (or parent) 
directory. This you do by running the chroot command as follows:

# chroot /mnt/sysimage
# _

Now you are in the shell with respect to the parent directory which is the 
linux partition on your harddisk.

>From here, the steps needed depends on which bootloader you are using. You 
have to have a fair idea what is the device node of your harddisk partition 
housing your MBR. In most cases, it is /dev/hda if you have an IDE harddisk. 
But if you have a SCSI harddisk, it will be /dev/sda.

Restoring GRUB
Execute the following command :

# grub-install /dev/hda

... to install GRUB boot loader on to your MBR. And then type exit to reboot 
the machine. Now your GRUB boot loader is fixed.

###NOTE### : Works with Fedora core.. Should work with any other distro 
also!!!

Regards,
Aanjhan

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Sat Dec 10 14:42:19 2005
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (Ramkumar R)
Date: Sat Dec 10 14:42:30 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] How to upgrade kernel and gcc
In-Reply-To: <twig.1134201508.7710@cdac.in>
References: <twig.1134201508.7710@cdac.in>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170512100112t4f1c8f23u8aa03de7b3f7d27c@mail.gmail.com>

> We need to upgrade kernel from 2.4 to 2.6 r higher and gcc from 3.3.5 to
> gcc 3.4 or higher in Debian ... Please send me the steps , how we can do
> this ...

just set your /etc/apt/sources.list file to include the sarge/etch
repositories and do a `apt-get dist-upgrade' (or alternatively, press
`u' in aptitude)

if u are doing a major update, it is suggested that you install
apt-listchanges before proceeding, this way you will get to know about
any changes that necessitate any manual changes.

regarding changing from 2.4 to 2.6, u just need to install the latest
kernel-image-2.6* package (for sarge) or linux-image-2.6* package (for
etch or later). make sure you recompile any local modules
(module-assistant takes care of module src packages installed using
debian, during the linux-image package installation)

hth :)

it moves on...

> note in the above it is /dev/hda or /dev/hdb not hda1 ...
>
> regards,
> kiran
>

I'ld recomment `mkfs -t ext3 /dev/whatever`.

grub-install shouldn't be required. Infact even if you use lilo, you will
not have to reinstall lilo on the MBR, since the partition table is intact.
mkfs changes only the partition's contents.
if you make changes to the partition table, then  you must rerun lilo.
unless you move grub's  files to a different partition, (or make changes
to the partition containing it,) I think you will not have to re-run
grub-install.

-Prakash.

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Sun Dec 11 07:59:43 2005
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Sun Dec 11 07:58:00 2005

In-Reply-To: <ff7d96f20512100757v4a8948ffj70bb5ae3b483775f@mail.gmail.com>

Message-ID: <20051211022943.GA1700@debian.home>

On Sat, Dec 10, 2005 at 09:27:18PM +0530, Rave Hanker wrote:
> 1. My sound driver fails , Prashanth Mohan tells me that the only way to do
> it to recompile the kernel(Yikes!) inorder to upgrade to the latest ALSA. Is
> there any other possibility

Yes. apt-get install linux-image-2.6.12-(686, smp etc.). 2.6.12 has
support for 915 sound as well as graphics. You don't need to recompile
the kernel, but you do need to boot nto the new kernel.

Kumar

Kumar Appaiah

> > I'ld recomment `mkfs -t ext3 /dev/whatever`.
> >
> > does this differ from
> > mke2fs -j
>
> Yes, its different.
>
> -j is for enabling journaling option in the
> filesystem, useful for better recovery.

Huh???

More precisely:

       -j     Create the filesystem with an ext3 journal.

which is exactly what mkfs -t ext3 would do. That is, ext3 = ext3. So
can you please explain how the two commands differ?

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sun Dec 11 23:42:20 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Mon Dec 12 13:12:32 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] remove windows
Message-ID: <20051212074220.45049.qmail@web50205.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Binand,

--- Binand wrote:
>       -j     Create the filesystem with an ext3
journal.
>
> which is exactly what mkfs -t ext3 would do. That
is, ext3 = 
> ext3. 
> So can you please explain how the two commands
differ?

Functionality wise they are the same. But, mkfs is a
wrap-around to other mkfs(.) calls. See the BUGS
section in man mkfs for its limitations. 

Its better to use tune2fs to convert ext2 to ext3
filesystems.

http://www.troubleshooters.com/linux/ext2toext3.htm

Cheers,

SK

From binand at gmail.com  Mon Dec 12 03:56:02 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Mon Dec 12 14:26:10 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] remove windows
In-Reply-To: <20051212074220.45049.qmail@web50205.mail.yahoo.com>

Message-ID: <d2a92d610512120056r3ca84bcbs@mail.gmail.com>

On 12/12/05, Shakthi Kannan <cyborg4k@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Functionality wise they are the same. But, mkfs is a
> wrap-around to other mkfs(.) calls. See the BUGS
> section in man mkfs for its limitations.

There is more to it. mkfs.ext3 and mke2fs are exactly the same program
- check their inode numbers and MD5 sums. I agree that mkfs -t foo
just calls mkfs.foo, but apart from the extra fork/exec overhead, I
cannot see any reason to recommend one over the other.

> Its better to use tune2fs to convert ext2 to ext3 filesystems.

That's for converting. For a fresh partition (which is what this
thread is all about), the way to go is mke2fs -j and equivalent, mkfs
-t ext3 (which are identical, no reason to recommend one over the
other).

Binand

Hi All,
There have been some discussions about this in tamil mailings lists and also
if remember correct in tamillinux mailing list also.

Right now many of the tamil authors are using the following terms:
Opensource -> Thira moolam ,
Opensource software -> Thira moola menporul

For Free software a good translation was given by one Dr.Irama.ki (
http://valavu.blogspot.com/ )
Free ==> pari  (means given free out of love without any strings attached to
it, read it similar to "parinthu koduthal" )
Free Software => Pari Niral or Pari Menporul

Also Dr.Irama.ki suggested "Thira Ootru" for Open Source  instead of Thira
Moolam
meaning Opensource software => Thira vootru menporul

Its upto us to adopt which ever is good :)

Regards,
Mugunth

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Mon Dec 12 02:44:04 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Mon Dec 12 16:14:12 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Wireless USB driver
In-Reply-To: <20051212085023.6BE041DB25A@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <20051212104404.59596.qmail@web50212.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Jagan,

--- Jagan <jaganra@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Anyone have any pointers on how this NDIS wrapper
> thing works. 

"Some vendors do not release specifications of the
hardware or provide a linux driver for their wireless
network cards. This project implements Windows kernel
API and NDIS (Network Driver Interface Specification)
API within Linux kernel. A Windows driver for wireless
network card is then linked to this implementation so
that the driver runs natively, as though it is in
Windows, without binary emulation.
"

Source: http://ndiswrapper.sourceforge.net/

> I have a wireless USB adapter 

Which one?

SK

Date: Mon Dec 12 17:39:50 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Redirecting a X display window to a null output
In-Reply-To: <70106e0b0512110201q114a13r4fa7e125547c8883@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20051212120257.7347.qmail@web8603.mail.in.yahoo.com>


--- Ingeneur <goda.abishek@gmail.com> wrote:

> Hi Haridh,
> 
> >   To be more clear, I have an application that loads on boot
> up(say GAIM,  i have it in rc.local). The gaim displays a window as
> soon as it loads.  I dont want the X window to be seen,(I need it
> to be redirected to a  null output). Now how do I do this?
> 
> The redirection is for standard streams. I don't think X is a
> stream!
> Well, correct me if not. Do you want to start "gaim" minimized?

You can use X Virtual frame buffer to redirect the GUI.

For example I some time run realplayer at command mode as follows

XVFB='Xvfb :2 -ac
export DISPLAY=:2
$XVFB 1>/dev/null 2>&1
realplay file.rm

The command Xvfb starts virtual frame buffer.

Raman.P

From andyetitmoves at gmail.com  Mon Dec 12 17:57:28 2005
From: andyetitmoves at gmail.com (Ramkumar R)
Date: Mon Dec 12 17:57:37 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Redirecting a X display window to a null output
In-Reply-To: <20051212065008.66509.qmail@web51409.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20051212065008.66509.qmail@web51409.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <9a9bfc170512120427h3e811907o6961d53ff0e23b11@mail.gmail.com>

> Thanks for the reply.It'l be nice if if i can start "gaim" minimized..tell me how..

that's the job of the window manager (though many apps provide an
option to do such "window manager"ly activities). enlightenment (which
I use) and many others provide this as an option on a window-by-window
basis...

> But it doesnt end with it. certain display windows cant be reduced or minimized.
> Like the ones when u open acroread, open office or lime wire. I actually want to prevent

what do u mean by they can't be minimized? could u please elucidate.
and if they "can't" be minimized, they can't be hidden as well...
because "minimized" is just hiding the window with a hint to the
window manager, so that it can put up some ui or icon in an iconbar or
something like that...

> Basically the user should not see what X window applications are loaded during startup (except from the system tray). Of course he can find it from rc.local!!

are you sure you want to load apps in rc.local? afaik, ~/.xsession is
a better place. rc.local starts the app as root and is meant for
services/commands which need to execute at startup and do not have a
dedicated file in /etc/init.d

it moves on...

From prem_sah1 at yahoo.com  Mon Dec 12 19:33:47 2005
From: prem_sah1 at yahoo.com (Premnath Sah)
Date: Tue Dec 13 09:03:59 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Regarding MBR and bootloader
In-Reply-To: <a54a308e0512120313n5b625445vadbae81b8de597b9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20051213033347.65992.qmail@web30115.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

Hi,

> do anybody know how to detect if Windows is
> installed in a system by reading
> the MBR?. 
> 
> any idea how to do it?
> 
> the only idea what i got is to mount fat32 or ntfs
> filesystems and search
> for windows directory....is that the right approach?
> 

See if this helps. MBR has info about four partitions
with one being set as bootable (bootable flag in
partition table). Check if this is set if it is set
then add a entry in boot loader. This is what bios
does to boot the system (loads the boot record from a
partition which is set as bootable if MBR has no
executable code).

regards
Premnath Sah T.H.

Dhanagopal Rengasamy wrote:
> It did not list the already existing
>  
>  C:    NTFS(10),
>  D:    FAT(10)
>  E:    FAT(10), 
>         ext3(MDK) and swap(10)
>   
It seems to be diskdrake's (Mandrake's disk partitioning tool) hand work
:-)  Diskdrake is so clever to manage any kind of partition. But the
worst part is, once diskdrake alter the partition table, many other
distro's or windows can't recognize the partition table properly
(atleast in my case - consistently). But existing partition will be
working properly. Other OS disk tools will show partition table as big
junk. e.g: Disk Manager of Windows shows that my HDD drive is of
capacity 40 GB (Yes,  perfect!), but the total size of all partition
comes 120GB (How can it be?). This is not the issue with Windows. Redhat
8.0 also did not recognize the partition table in this case. Debian too.

My suggestion is to check the partition table from Windows (if u want to
retain windows). Delete the MDK (after backup if any) partitions and
ensure that windows shows proper valid partition table. Then you install
Ubuntu. Finally you consider MDK if you want.

-- 
Regards,
T.KaruppuSwamy

On Mon, 2005-12-12 at 18:22, Rajagopal Natarajan wrote:
> It is not generally advisable to use softmodems. The softmodems give
> away some of their modem work to the CPU. They dont have any innate
> intelligence that the 'true' modems posses. The manufacturers exploit
> the fact that Winlows ppl dont normally do multitasking. So the users
> dont find much difference in speed while using those softmodems.
> Whereas if you would do true multitasking (or) run a program that
> would exploit the maximum potency of your processor, you lose some
> part of the processor to your modem, due to its lack built-in of
> intelligence. Though manufacturing of softmodems is far far cheaper
> than the 'intelligent' modems (which have the chipset to do the work
> of a modem), the commercial benefit is not given to the consumer. The
> manufacturers price them approx equal to the intelligent ones.
> Its better for you to change your plan and buy a truemodem, instead of
> a soft one.
>

Hi,

> from the bootable flag,can i find Windows is
> installed or not?

Iam not familiar with the bootloader of windows. you
may check whether any unique signature is found on the
windows bootloader.

What I wanted to express was immaterial of any OS
being installed the user expects your bootloader to
have a entry. You can blindly assume that FAT32/NTFS
contains Windows if its bootable flag is set

Check this output of "fdisk -l"

Disk /dev/hda: 40.0 GB, 40060403712 bytes
255 heads, 63 sectors/track, 4870 cylinders
Units = cylinders of 16065 * 512 = 8225280 bytes

   Device Boot      Start         End      Blocks   Id
 System
/dev/hda1   *           1          13      104391   83
 Linux
/dev/hda2              14          78      522112+  82
 Linux swap
/dev/hda3              79        4870    38491740   83
 Linux

here /dev/hda1 is bootable and filesystem is some
linux filesystem because the Id is 83 and hence you
can add an entry in bootloader for this partitiion.

Premnath Sah T.H.

From binand at gmail.com  Tue Dec 13 15:04:24 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Wed Dec 14 01:35:06 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Regarding MBR and bootloader
In-Reply-To: <a54a308e0512120313n5b625445vadbae81b8de597b9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <a54a308e0512120313n5b625445vadbae81b8de597b9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610512131204j77f374c9r@mail.gmail.com>

On 12/12/05, Chakkaradeep C C <chaks.yoper@gmail.com> wrote:
> do anybody know how to detect if Windows is installed in a system by reading
> the MBR?. I am adding the bootloader option in the Yoper Installer,so for

Here is a little proglet I had posted a long time ago on
linux-india-programmers. Adapting it to detect Windows left as an
exercise to the reader :)

Usage:

1. Save the code into bootloader.c
2. Compile it - make bootloader
3. Run it - ./bootloader /dev/hda (use your disk here)

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <unistd.h>
#include <fcntl.h>

int main(int argc, char **argv) {
        char *dev = argv[1];
        char buf[4];
        int fd;
        fd = open (dev, O_RDONLY);
        if (fd < 0) {
                perror ("open");
                exit (1);
        }
        if (lseek (fd, 6, SEEK_SET) < 0) {
                perror ("lseek");
                exit (1);
        }
        if (read (fd, buf, 4) != 4) {
                perror ("read");
                exit (1);
        }
        if (buf[0] == 0x4c && buf[1] == 0x49 && buf[2] == 0x4c &&
buf[3] == 0x4f) {
                printf ("Boot Loader is LILO\n");
        } else {
                printf ("Other Boot Loader - Possibly Grub\n");
        }
        close(fd);
        return 0;
}
From binand at gmail.com  Tue Dec 13 15:04:24 2005

On 12/12/05, Chakkaradeep C C <chaks.yoper@gmail.com> wrote:
> do anybody know how to detect if Windows is installed in a system by reading
> the MBR?. I am adding the bootloader option in the Yoper Installer,so for

Here is a little proglet I had posted a long time ago on
linux-india-programmers. Adapting it to detect Windows left as an
exercise to the reader :)

Usage:

1. Save the code into bootloader.c
2. Compile it - make bootloader
3. Run it - ./bootloader /dev/hda (use your disk here)

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <unistd.h>
#include <fcntl.h>

int main(int argc, char **argv) {
        char *dev = argv[1];
        char buf[4];
        int fd;
        fd = open (dev, O_RDONLY);
        if (fd < 0) {
                perror ("open");
                exit (1);
        }
        if (lseek (fd, 6, SEEK_SET) < 0) {
                perror ("lseek");
                exit (1);
        }
        if (read (fd, buf, 4) != 4) {
                perror ("read");
                exit (1);
        }
        if (buf[0] == 0x4c && buf[1] == 0x49 && buf[2] == 0x4c &&
buf[3] == 0x4f) {
                printf ("Boot Loader is LILO\n");
        } else {
                printf ("Other Boot Loader - Possibly Grub\n");
        }
        close(fd);
        return 0;
}

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Dec 14 10:58:20 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Dec 14 10:56:05 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (DISPLAY)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0512141057390.4024-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

OSSRC-India (Open Source Software Resource Centre) is started to  
Foster significant OSS development and promotion of Open Standards
in India. URL: http://www.ossrc.org.in/

One Day One Command (By Mr Arpit Sud)
======================================

display -- Display an Image on any workstation running X.

Summary:

Display is a machine architecture independent image processing and
display program. It can display an image on any workstation screen
running an X server. Display can read and write many of the more
popular image formats (e.g. JPEG, TIFF, PNM, Photo CD, etc.). It has 
many option to perform operation like invert, resize, rotate, etc..

Examples:

$ display image.jpg -- Display the image.jpg.

$ display -size 800x640 image.png -- Display the image.png in 800x640 
                                     pixels.

$ display -colors 16 image.gif -- Display the image.gif as a 16bit 
                                 colors image.

$ display -border 10x10 -bordercolor red  image.png -- Display the 
                   image with red color border of size 10x10 pixels.

$ display http://www.chennailug.org/pictures/titlealt.jpg -- Display 
                                              the image from the URL.

$ display -monochrome colors.png -- Display the color image in 
                                    monochrome format.

Read: man display

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

I think Linus is right about this; Gnome has regressed in many ways - some
of the older versions of Gnome were actually easier to use than the new
versions coming out. The file selection dialog is absolutely horrible from
a usability perspective and I find it hard to believe that the Gnome
developers believe that it is actually makes it easier for newbie users.
The KDE file dialog is a whole lot smarter in my humble opinion. Nautilus
is also not really intuitive.

Also regarding Linus voicing his opinion - surely he is entitled to one?
and surely he can voice it in a forum dealing with that exact subject?
Anyone is welcome to disagree with him.

Please note that I am not a KDE fanboy - I use Linux a lot and it powers
most of the computers here at work. I use both Gnome and KDE but I am
increasingly getting frustrated with the UI design appearing in Gnome.
Many of these changes are not intuitive and frankly irritating - take for
instance the "spatial" display used in Nautilus. It is horrible in my
opinion.

Ok, I think I have stirred up enough controversy here. You can start
flaming away challenging me to write a better desktop environment.

Prem Kurian Philip
Songbird Technologies

Hi,

--- Binand Sethumadhavan <binand@gmail.com> wrote:
> I use a Prolific PL2303 converter and am pretty
> happy with it.

I bought a Bafo Technologies, BF-810 USB to serial
converter at Mercy Electronics, L.B. Road, Chennai for
around Rs.450/-. It uses the PL-2303 driver. I also
bought a serial port DB-9 female to DB-9 female
converter for around Rs.50/-. 

The converter and cable come with a CD which has the
PL-2303 Linux drivers for 2.4 for Redhat 9. But, the
packaging cover only specifies drivers for winblow$.
Huh! The stock kernel sources already have the latest
drivers.

I compiled drivers/usb/serial/usbserial.ko and
drivers/usb/serial/pl2303.ko and loaded them on
2.6.12.3. It was detected fine and /dev/ttyUSB0 was
created!

Thanks to Binand and Vijairaj for their suggestions.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Thu Dec 15 10:33:53 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Thu Dec 15 10:31:21 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (COMPOSITE)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0512151033180.4976-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Live GNU/Linux CDs are very useful to learn about the OS, with-out
installing in the Hard disk. Here is the list of Live CDs, 
URL: http://www.frozentech.com/content/livecd.php (Thanks FN).

One Day One Command (By Mr Arpit Sud)
======================================

composite -- Composite images together.

Summary:

Composite is used composite/combine/mix images to create new images.
It is a part of the ImageMagick utilities (www.imagemagick.org).

Examples:

$ composite A.jpg B.jpg C.jpg -- Composite A with B and store the 
                                 result in C.

$ composite -compose difference A.png B.png C.png -- Compute the 
              difference between A and B, and store the result in C.

$ composite -geometry +100+150 A.png B.png C.png -- Place A at 
             specified location with B and store the result in C.

$ composite -dissolve 20 A.jpg B.jpg C.jpg -- Dissolve A 20% and mix 
                                   with B, and store the result in C.

$ composite -rotate 40 A.jpg B.png C.gif -- Rotate A 40 Degree and mix 
                                    with B and store the result in C.

Read: man composite

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Fri Dec 16 12:00:21 2005
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy)
Date: Fri Dec 16 11:56:32 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] My first experience with FreeBSD
Message-ID: <43A25EFD.3040908@tandbintl.com>

I have installed FreeBSD 6.0 in my laptop HP nx6120. I have configured
as desktop system during install time. The boot time seems to be quite
fast. Since I have only one CD, the base system has been installed.
packages adding is cool with pkg_add tool. Then I installed afterstep
desktop through ftp, to check the X windows performance. If you have
already worked in linux, FreeBSD is very easy. I thought it was more
server oriented. But it has given me a good knock of proving that
suitable for desktop also. The linux compatibility makes FreeBSD to
utilize the linux based application development. A plenty of application
choice is there to install (as packages and ports). Disk partition tool
highlights slice concept other than partition. The device naming
conventions are slightly different from linux. It follows Debian way of
install (but going back and forth in installation phase is not as
flexible as debian).

Hardware compatibility for my HP nx6120 laptop:
------------------------------------------------------------------
ACPI works just like that without any tweak.
Audio card works without any tweak.
Display works without any tweak.
Network card works without any tweak.
Wireless, Bluetooth and IrDA detected - Not yet tested.

-- 
Regards,
T.KaruppuSwamy,

From binand at gmail.com  Fri Dec 16 04:50:12 2005

Subject: [Ilugc] Network Traffic Monitor
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0512151919250.12193-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

On 15/12/05, Bharathi Subramanian <sbharathi@midascomm.com> wrote:
> Basically I have nearly 50PCs in my network. I want monitor the
> network by sniffing the packets and plot the usage graph, at X min
> resolution, for each IP address. It is good if the usage splited into
> protocols, like HTTP, FTP,...

Ah well. Here goes.

What you want to do is called traffic accounting. Typically, the
device on a network that sees ALL traffic is the backbone switching
device - hence traffic accounting is done there. And since more often
than not the backbone device is from Cisco, the technology used is
Cisco Netflow.

On the other hand, if you want to do this only at your border, you can
have a Netflow probe on your border router (the PC :) and a Netflow
collector running on a different box (or even the same one, but
depending on traffic Netflow collection puts quite a high demand on
CPU and storage).

The best-known GPL'ed implementation of a Netflow probe is nProbe from
the guys who wrote ntop.  It is homed at
http://www.ntop.org/nProbe.html. There are several commercial Netflow
analyzers available, google for them - or you could use ntop for a
GPL'ed Netflow collector. Graphing is usually done by RRDTool in
GPL'ed environments.

It is not an easy thing to setup; you need to have exceptional
understanding of TCP/IP and OSI layers (especially layer 2 and layer
3).

Binand

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Sat Dec 17 10:46:27 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Sat Dec 17 10:44:00 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (IDENTIFY)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0512171046030.22178-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

MIT OCW (Open Course Ware), An open educational resource published
on-line by faculties of MIT, who choose to share their research,
pedagogy & knowledge to benefit others. URL: http://ocw.mit.edu/

One Day One Command (By Mr Arpit Sud)
======================================

identify -- Describe an image.

Summary:

Identify describes the format and characteristics of one or more image
files. It will also report if an image is incomplete or corrupt.  The
information displayed includes the scene number, the file name, the
width and height of the image, whether the image is color mapped or
not, the number of colors in the image, the number of bytes in the
image, the format of the image (JPEG, PNM, etc.), and finally the
number of seconds it took to read and process the image.

It is a part of the ImageMagick utilities (www.imagemagick.org).

Examples:

$ identify img.png -- Show short info about the image.

$ identify a.miff b.png c.jpg d.gif -- Show short info about all 
                                       image files.

$ identify -verbose img.jpg -- Show detailed info about the image.

Read: man identify

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Dec 17 11:01:04 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Dec 18 00:31:43 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [Photos] Ruby talk, Vamsee, December 17, 2005
Message-ID: <20051217190105.1293.qmail@web50203.mail.yahoo.com>

Greetings!

The photos taken during Vamsee's talk on "Ruby" at Ma
Foi Academy, Chennai on Saturday, December 17, 2005
can be viewed from:

http://www.shakthimaan.com/Mambo/gallery/album22

MoM, Saturday, December 17, 2005, 1500 hrs IST
----------------------------------------------

* We started at 1500 hrs IST, and were initially
discussing about restrictions to hostel students at a
university in Chennai. Why computing freedom was not
given to these students, because one/two were
mischievous. Students had got permission to setup a
LAN at their hostel, they paid from their pockets, and
set everything up, only to be forced to dismantle the
setup. Obsolete college admins who don't care for
education or know to use technology. Huh! We had
discussions on possibility of bluetooth LAN or
wireless LANs connection via USB for the students.

* Deepan had some doubts with joomla (formerly,
Mambo), and we walked through the administrator
interface (live!) and had discussions on components,
modules, section, categories in joomla.

* Vamsee began the talk at 1600 hrs IST and
illustrated the coding style and features of Ruby. He
also talked about Ruby on Rails and  showed us good
documentation for learning Ruby.

http://poignantguide.net/ruby/

http://tryruby.hobix.com/

* Vamsee ordered some puffs and coffee/tea and we had
a good munch. He also showed the photos taken at
foss.in and shared his foss.in experience with us. 

* Meanwhile, one Bharanidharan from geminfotech met me
at Ma Foi, and said he was sorry that his folks had
sent spam e-mails to all ilugc members. Hmmmm. He
wanted to know what he could do for ilugc or sponsor
us for any events. Sounded more like commercial to me.
I asked him to attend LUG meetings and first get to
know of our voluntary work for the benefit of society.


* We were then catching up with news in the FLOSS
world. Google recruits came up in our discussion:

http://www.google.co.in/jobs/positions-in.html

* We finished at 1830 hrs IST.

I hope I have covered everything. Please feel free to
add to the above.

Happy Ruby (and duck :) hacking,

SK

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Dec 17 11:22:58 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Dec 18 00:53:12 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] codecoolies meet
In-Reply-To: <8816fcf80512171033m699832deh62c23f71bb149815@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20051217192258.41178.qmail@web50209.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Sridhar, Kenneth Gonsalves and others,

Firstly, kudos to Kenneth Gonsalves for taking an
initiative, codecoolies.

> Ooty

Summer 2006?

> Hm.. why not have it in a central place where it is
> easier for people to
> travel to. 

Any suggestions?

> Don't we have more open source developers
> in Bangalore than any
> other city? 

Well. We also have to cater to other cities/remote
places because:

1. There are people in rural areas who cannot afford
to travel to the cities. But, you and me _can_
definitely afford to travel to these places.

2. Having an event in a town/small city gives the
people there an opportunity to market themselves. Some
companies might even want to setup bases in these
places. For example, Honeywell Technologies has an R&D
center in Madurai.  It reduces the pressure on big
cities. Yes, I know about Bangalore traffic.

3. The event bridges the gap between academia and the
industry. Institutes like IIT, in the city, have a
fantastic collaboration with the industry. How many
colleges/institutions in towns/small cities have such
collaboration? Give them an opportunity. The event can
give them contacts for them to establish themselves
well and make a name for themselves.

Having an 2/3-day event in a college is ideal. "Tuxedo
2005" or "Carte Blanche 2005" are good examples. They
were a mixture of contests for students, industry
talks, stalls, fun and frolic!

> I believe the first meet should happen
> in a popular place.

Place doesn't matter. Its the people behind the event
that really matter.

SK

Subject: [Ilugc] Linux on T41

It is that triennial event here - I will get a new business laptop,
and also an option of buying the old one at a much reduced price (this
time the new one is going to be a T42, with fingerprint reader and
whatnot - sweet! :). So I have decided to get back to desktop Linux.
The last time I had one was way back in 2001 - Redhat 7.1, I think.

So I know that a lot of water has flown under the bridge. Kernel is
now at 2.6.x, KDE is 3.5, GCC 3.x, etc. etc. At the moment, I am
considering two options for the distro:

1. OpenSUSE 10 - I have the ISOs downloaded and burnt. I can start
installation today.
2. Fedora Core 5 - wait for it. :)

So I have these questions.

1. I'd want to retain the dual-boot option for the time being. Do I
still have to fiddle around with fips.exe or do modern installers
handle it on their own? The full disk at the moment is on NTFS with
Windows XP SP2 Pro as the OS.
2. Hardware compatibility - Wifi and Infrared, mainly. Wifi it seems
is fully supported, but I haven't seen much discussion about IR.
3. Suspend and hibernate?
4. My camera - Canon IXUS 500.
5. Other assorted USB stuff I have accumulated over time - a Belkin
USB hub, an IBM and a Logitec USB 2-button mouses (mice?) with scroll
wheels, my iPAQ PDA, my Sandisk USB thumb drive etc.
6. My Nokia 6820 mobile phone, via IR (Gnokii?).
7. Does the Thinkpad keyboard work fully? There are several Fn+key
options on the keyboard, plus an extra pair of Forward/Backward keys
on either side of the up-arrow key.

I don't think I'll have a problem with Internet access - my 3Com
ADSL/Wifi router is mostly plug and play with all the providers I have
tried it so far.

The laptop is a Thinkpad T41 with 1GB RAM. I did look at
linux-laptop.net but almost all the reviews there are for Linux-only
boots. I tried a couple of live CDs (Knoppix and Kubuntu), and I am of
the opinion that KDE does look good on this laptop.

Binand
From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Dec 17 22:12:56 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Dec 18 11:43:03 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Linux on T41
