Hi Binand,

--- Binand Sethumadhavan <binand@gmail.com> wrote:
> The full disk at the moment
> is on NTFS with
> Windows XP SP2 Pro as the OS.

You could have partitioned the hard disk on first
power up, when the hard disk was at fat32, the default
factory setting. winblow$ converts the entire
partition to ntfs on first boot. Duh!

> 2. Hardware compatibility - Wifi and Infrared,
> mainly. Wifi it seems
> is fully supported, 

Yes. I use ipw2100 on my T41. No monitor mode
operation for this chipset though.

http://ipw2100.sourceforge.net/

Yours could be the ipw2200.

http://ipw2200.sourceforge.net/

> but I haven't seen much
> discussion about IR.

Which model is it? ... (1)

> 3. Suspend and hibernate?

Good in 2.6.x. 

> 4. My camera - Canon IXUS 500.

Supported, both normal mode and PTP mode.

http://www.gphoto.org/proj/libgphoto2/support.php

> 5. Other assorted USB stuff I have accumulated over
> time - a Belkin
> USB hub, an IBM and a Logitec USB 2-button mouses
> (mice?) with scroll
> wheels, 

Not sure about mice. I prefer to use the trackpoint on
the T41. 

> my iPAQ PDA, 

Does this help?

http://lwn.net/2001/0607/desktop.php3

> my Sandisk USB thumb drive etc.

Sandisks have good support for GNU/Linux. I use their
256 MB flash drives on Debian 2.6.12.

> 6. My Nokia 6820 mobile phone, via IR (Gnokii?).

See (1) above.

> 7. Does the Thinkpad keyboard work fully? There are
> several Fn+key
> options on the keyboard, plus an extra pair of
> Forward/Backward keys
> on either side of the up-arrow key.

You can always configure the key mappings?

You might also want to post your questions to
linux-thinkpad mailing list:

http://mailman.linux-thinkpad.org/mailman/listinfo/linux-thinkpad

Have fun,

SK

doesn't meen that they are embracing open source (read: yet not).  The point
I'm trying to make is a LUG should be a LUG. It is *local* Linux users
group. As long as the discussions pertain to locality, solving problems
being faced by users and any general stuff related to Linux and open source,
I feel, that would contribute more towards growth.

I mean, all such philosophy, general discussions can be had on many other
mailing lists like fsf-general, etc ... A LUG should be a LUG. We have
slashdot for what it is mean to be.

If that has concerns on freedom, ilugc-general would suffice. :-)

--
Sridhar Ratna - http://srid.multiply.com/

Subject: [Ilugc] Mapping keys of my Laptop
In-Reply-To: <BAY110-F288760E2C8B355A5B0BBD9B3C0@phx.gbl>

   Aanjhan R wrote:

     I would like to know how to map my COMPAQ Laptop keys to certain
     functions

   When you press a key, a scan code is read by kernel. In case of special
   keys, you have to map with "setkeycodes" command. To know the
   corresponding key code for your key, refer dmesg after pressing a key.

From vamlists at gmx.net  Mon Dec 19 10:44:38 2005
From: vamlists at gmx.net (Vamsee Kanakala)
Date: Mon Dec 19 10:43:49 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Mapping keys of my Laptop
In-Reply-To: <BAY110-F288760E2C8B355A5B0BBD9B3C0@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY110-F288760E2C8B355A5B0BBD9B3C0@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <43A641BE.5020002@gmx.net>

Aanjhan R wrote:

> The Vol Up,Down,Mute buttons to the respective functions
>
Normally this should work independent of the OS - at least, it is so in 
my Thinkpad.

> The M$ Wdws key to some function (is lying waste) --> Any suggestions??
>
There should be a provision to map it to something useful in Gnome - 
don't know about KDE. I mapped the left one (0x73) to firefox and right 
one (0x74) to thunderbird in my desktop - thankfully, the thinkpad 
doesn't have M$ keys.

> And my wireless button to enable wireless in my Laptop
>
Is it working otherwise? If it's a centrino, you need ipw2200 drivers. 
If it's Atheros chipset based, you need Madwifi. If the wireless card is 
not detected & configured automatically by your distro, you need to 
recompile your kernel with the above drivers and muck around with 
wpa_supplicant. Google is your friend. I heard that Ubuntu is a very 
good laptop distro and is good with wireless. I use Debian, so can't say.

Linux on laptop is not yet the joy it is to install on a desktop, so be 
prepared to get your hands dirty. So far, I haven't configured suspend 
to RAM/HDD on my laptop. My experiments with ibm-acpi put the laptop in 
suspend but it won't get back when I open the lid, so I abandoned that 
project for now. The wireless however, works flawlessly.


Vamsee.

Hi,

> The Vol Up,Down,Mute buttons to the respective functions

I have a HP/Compaq nx5000, on which I installed Ubuntu Breezy a couple
of weeks back, and surprisingly all these keys were automatically
mapped - the volume up, down and mute that is.

> The M$ Wdws key to some function (is lying waste) --> Any suggestions??

This key usually translates to Super_L or Super_R or something like
that. I use that key to open the "Run" dialog(i.e, Alt+F2 dialog) in
Gnome. It cannot however be used as a modifer key I think(atleast on
gnome).

> And my wireless button to enable wireless in my Laptop

This worked out of the box too! It enables and disables wireless flawlessly.

I havent tried the suspend thing though, so no clue on that one.

I was quite surprised with how well Ubuntu worked actually - was
definitely a joy to install (probably a different kind of joy, from
that described by shakthi! ).

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Mon Dec 19 16:06:57 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Mon Dec 19 16:00:53 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [Fwd: [PRC] C, C++, lex, yacc, assembly BASIC,
 LOGO etc. in Hindi, Bangla and other vernaculars]

-------- Original Message --------
Subject: 	[PRC] C, C++, lex, yacc, assembly BASIC, LOGO etc. in Hindi, 
Bangla and other vernaculars
Date: 	Mon, 19 Dec 2005 08:41:00 +0530 (IST)
From: 	Abhishek Choudhary <choudhary@indicybers.net>
Reply-To: 	Free/Libre and Open Source Software Project List <prc@sarai.net>
To: 	prc@sarai.net



Respected Sir/Madam,

This is to inform you of the availability of the first ever "complete" 
suite of open-source programming languages for Indian vernaculars. It 
includes equivalents of C, C++, lex, yacc, assembly, Java etc. in Hindi, 
Bangla and other vernaculars. Along with this I have also released Hindi 
and Bangla DOS, including BASIC and Logo for vernaculars. The downloads are 
available at http://www.indicybers.com

These projects have won Computer Society of India's Young IT Professional 
Award (Eastern region) 2005 (Winner) and 2004 (Special mention), two years 
in a row. I shall be competing at the 2005 national level now.

Some of the innovations of this project include a system for displaying 
Indic scripts in "true" text-mode. This is done without using any aditional 
hardware. At no point has any graphical (rasterising) method been used for 
this. All the required glyphs have been accomodated in the extended ASCII 
code page, leaving 7-bit ASCII unaltered. This method is applicable to all 
Brahmi derived composite syllabic Indian scripts. Hindi, Bangla, Assamese 
and Gujrati scripts have been implemented. Oriya and Punjabi are under 
development. There are strong suggestions that this may be applicable for 
South Indian scripts as well. This has made it possible to have BIOS/POST 
in Indic. Besides, this system being free, it does not add to the 
procurement cost as compared to commercial products.

Another contribution of this project includes a "case and diacritic 
independent, compiler acceptable" transliteration system. This is 
completely invertible and is applicable to all Indian languages. This has 
direct mapping to the IPA and, hence, may be used to develop programming 
languages in "any" human language. It also has bearings on web technology,  
as it can allow Indic URLs in IPv4 as well. It may be used to encode even 
static web-pages, such that if someone does not have the required fonts 
then one may see the Indic web-page in Roman script transliteration, 
instead of "boxes" (unicode) or garbage (other encodings), from the 
same "static" html.

Finally, the task of Indic programming language design has not been trivial 
either. I have also included support for HP printers. The system uses GCC 
as back-end and is highly portable. There is both ISCII and UNICODE support 
for all languages, including Hindi/Bangla DOS and the IDE. Necessary 
filters have been provided for conversions between ISCII, Romenagri, 
UNICODE, APCISR, HP-PCL etc. The languages have been developed 
synchronically and, hence, there is a certain level of homogenity in 
keyword selection across paradigms. The programs written in Indic 
programming languages are readily converted to their English equivalents 
and hence may be delivered internationally. There is also support for 
translation of variable names and rudimentary literate programming. 
Unreleased languages include Lisp, Prolog, Ada, Pascal, Fortran etc. in 
Inian vernaculars. They shall be released soon, after the initial testing 
and verification of license issues. However the availability of lex and 
yacc makes the issues of targeting specific lanuages quite trivial, and 
these are already available for download along with C, C++, assembly, 
BASIC, logo, and Java in Hindi and Bangla.

Technologically, Hindi/Bangla C/C++/assembly has been used for robotics and 
cluster super-computers. Along with this system, I have also released in 
public domain the design of a natural-interfaced autonomous robot. The 
languages have also been used to successfully implement a Beowulf cluster. 
Effort is now being made towards porting Linux kernel sources to 
Hindi/Bangla C, asm etc. This is aided by the fact that I have also include 
English-programming-language to Hindi/Bangla-programming-language 
translators and vice-versa.

Sir/Madam, I have released all this software as free open source for the 
greater benefit of the vernacular literate population of our country. I do 
not have any financial interests from it. However, I shall appreciate 
support in any form (including coding, awareness, maintainance, and 
financial). I am also looking for a suitable job. My experience includes 
systems programming (compiler design, device drivers, Linux kernel), 
computational linguistics, embedded systems, C/C++/assembly/Java, medical-
informatics, artificial intelligence, and technical writing. 

Link to my resume: http://indicybers.com/abhishek/

Link to my degree thesis: http://indicybers.com/hindawi/ANGELBot.pdf

Link for downloading Indic programming languages: http://www.indicybers.com

Link for downloading Indic programming languages paper: 
http://indicybers.com/hindawi/Hindawi.pdf

Link for downloading Indic programming languages presentation: 
http://indicybers.com/hindawi/Hindawi.ppt

Regards,
Abhishek Choudhary

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Dec 19 22:20:40 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Dec 19 22:17:37 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One GNU/Linux Command (MOGRIFY)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0512192220150.22190-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Kernel Janitors is a project to help a person, who want to be kernel
hackers, get their feet wet, while doing something useful for the
community. URL: http://janitor.kernelnewbies.org/ (Thanks Ringo)

One Day One Command (By Mr Arpit Sud)
======================================

mogrify -- Mogrify an image

Summary:

Mogrify transforms an image or a sequence of images. These transforms
include image scaling, image rotation, color reduction, and others.

NOTE: The transmogrified image overwrites the original image, unless
an option such as -format causes the output filename to be different
from the input filename.

It is a part of the ImageMagick utilities (www.imagemagick.org).

Examples:

$ mogrify -format jpeg *.tiff -- Convert all the TIFF files in a 
                                 current Dir to JPEG.

$ mogrify -resize 120x120 +profile '*' *.png -- Convert all PNG files 
                                                to 120x120 Size.

Read: man mogrify

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

Dear shakti,

My thoughts below,

I do acknowledge your concerns of little being done(by some of its
members) to spread linux or contributing to FLOSS activities. But
don't you think linux would spread ( should i say should speard) on
its own merits. Think of the day, what would happens if there not
enough linux supporters in TN. Would linux not exist in TN. Further
bandwith or load on the mailling list server at iitm should not be a
cause of serious concern so as to stop such posting. Definitely you &
me & many others over here are on broadband. Regarding load on iitm
server, there is not much traffic at iitm to cause concern. We
definetly don't get as many mails as at fedora or debian mail server (
AFAIK these distros are mainly community based with some industry
support). AFAIK server at iitm are sufficiently well built to handle
this traffic. The bandwith problems could true during the days of
dialup connection. I find that argument no longer holds true. I think
policing the list will not contribute to ilugc or linux.

with regards.
ashwin

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Tue Dec 20 21:02:21 2005

Hi,

--- Anandh G <anandhg02@yahoo.com> wrote:
>   1. I want to know if solaris 10 has good hardware
> compatiblity than Linux.

What hardware? You have to be specific.
    
>   2. Is there difference between the various Linux
> Distro in hardware compatiblity. Like for example,
> Redhat will support one device and SuSe won't
> support that device.

Let's get to the basics.

Distros differ mainly in their package management
system. Hardware support is dependant on the Linux
kernel, not the distro as such. What vendors do is
just pick a stock kernel (from kernel.org) and
customize it. Even then, you can still run different
kernels on different distros. 
 
SK

From: chaks.yoper at gmail.com (Chakkaradeep C C)
Date: Wed Dec 21 11:37:13 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Year 2038 problem - real?
Message-ID: <a54a308e0512202207oc7976b8i1d2c4d58cb3f7d1d@mail.gmail.com>

i got this mail,but didnt try...is it real???


*Year 2038..Again the replica of Y2K*

Note: This is just for FYI only, Please Don't try

this. This is true and  if you do this then your

network based applications will not work.

The Year 2038 Problem

Triaging steps...

1. login to yahoo messenger

2. send instant message to anyone - fine its

working...

3. now, change your system date to 19-Jan-2038,

03:14:07 AM or above

4. Confirm weather your date is changed

5. again send instant message to anyone...



Your YM crashes....



* * * YES ALL NETWORK BASED APPLICATION WILL NOT WORK

NOW * * *



*Why.....

What is it?*



Starting at GMT 03:14:07, Tuesday, January 19, 2038,

It is expected to see lots of systems around the world

breaking magnificently: satellites falling out of

orbit, massive power outages (like the 2003 North

American black out), hospital life support system

failures, phone system interruptions, banking errors,

etc. One second after this critical second, many of

these systems will have wildly inaccurate date

settings, producing all kinds of unpredictable

consequences. In short, many of the dire predictions

for the year 2000 are much more likely to actually

occur in the year 2038! Consider the year 2000 just a

dry run. In case you think we can sit on this issue

for another 30 years before addressing it, consider

that reports of temporal echoes of the 2038 problem

are already starting to appear in future date

calculations for mortgages and vital statistics!

In the first month of the year 2038 C.E. many

computers will encounter a date-related bug in their

operating systems and/or in the applications they run.

This can result in incorrect and wildly inaccurate

dates being reported by the operating system and/or

applications. The effect of this bug is hard to

predict, because many applications are not prepared

for the resulting "skip" in reported time anywhere

from 1901 to a "broken record" repeat of the reported

time at the second the bug occurs. Also, may make

some small adjustment to the actual time the bug

expresses itself. This bug to cause serious problems

on many platforms, especially Unix and Unix-like

platforms, because these systems will "run out of

time".

What causes it?

Time_t is a data type used by C and C++ programs to

represent dates and times internally. (Windows

programmers out there might also recognize it as the

basis for the CTime and CTimeSpan classes in MFC.)

time_t is actually just an integer, a whole number,

that counts the number of seconds since January 1,

1970 at 12:00 AM Greenwich Mean Time. A time_t value

of 0 would be 12:00:00 AM (exactly midnight)

1-Jan-1970, a time_t value of 1 would be 12:00:01 AM

(one second after midnig ht) 1-Jan-1970, etc..

some example times and their exact time_t

representations:

Date & time time_t representation

1-Jan-1970, 12:00:00 AM GMT 0

1-Jan-1970, 12:01:00 AM GMT 60

1-Jan-1970, 01:00:00 AM GMT 3 600

2-Jan-1970, 12:00:00 AM GMT 86 400

1-Jan-1971, 12:00:00 AM GMT 31 536 000

1-Jan-1972, 12:00:00 AM GMT 63 072 000

1-Jan-2038, 12:00:00 AM GMT 2 145 916 800

19-Jan-2038, 03:14:07 AM GMT 2 147 483 647

By the year 2038, the time_t representation for the

current time will be over 2 140 000 000. And that's

the problem. A modern 32-bit computer stores a "signed

integer" data type, such as time_t, in 32 bits. The

first of these bits is used for the positive/negative

sign of the integer, while the remaining 31 bits are

used to store the number itself.

The highest number these 31 data bits can store works

out to exactly 2 147 483 647. A time_t value of this

exact number, 2 147 483 647, represents Janu ary 19,

2038, at 7 seconds past 3:14 AM Greenwich Mean Time.

So, at 3:14:07 AM GMT on that fateful day, every

time_t used in a 32-bit C or C++ program will reach

its upper limit.

One second later, on 19-January-2038 at 3:14:08 AM

GMT, disaster  strikes.  When a signed integer reaches

its maximum value and then gets incremented, it wraps

around to its lowest possible negative value. This

means a 32-bit signed integer, such as a time_t, set

to its maximum value of 2 147 483 647 and then

incremented by 1, will become -2 147 483 648. Note

that "-" sign at the beginning of this large number. A

time_t value of -2 147 483 648 would represent

December 13, 1901 at 8:45:52 PM GMT.

So, if all goes normally, 19-January-2038 will

suddenly become 13-December-1901 in every time_t

across the globe, and every date calculation based on

this figure will go haywire. And it gets worse. Most

of the support functions that use t he time_t data type

cannot handle negative time_t values at all. They

simply fail and return an error code.

To both:

HP Proliant DL360 series servers are really, really good. 1U
rack-mountable servers, with 2 x U320 SCSI disks (more recently HP has
added a SATA option in their DL360 G4 series) in a hardware raid
config - you could use raid0 and get storage of both disks combined or
raid1 to get redundancy. HP's PSP (Proliant Support Pack) comes only
in RHEL or SLES versions, though. You might want to reconsider the
Distro. The amount of perfomance these servers give me are truly
amazing. Has lights-out management and WOL out of the box.

IBM and Dell are other options you can try.

NAS: Did you mean direct attached storage boxes? Any NAS box that
supports NFS/CIFS can be used with Linux.

Binand

Dear Binand, Sudharshan and others,

--- Binand wrote:
> Solaris 10 is software. Linux is software. So where
does 
> hardware come into this picture?

As on date and AFAIK, you can't run software in the
air. It has to run on some piece of hardware. Hence,
hardware is important and we cannot make assumptions
on it. 

--- Sudharshan S <sudharsh@gmail.com> wrote:
> doesnt different
> distros have
> different styles for customizing the vannila
> kernel..if i can recollect,

There is no style as such. They customize it, yes.
Sometimes, they don't even ship the sources in the
installation CD (was it FC3 or FC4?). So, when end
users try to build drivers, they are faced with
problems. Ok, things are good with Ubuntu and its
hardware detection, its an exception. Newbies also
forget to install gcc required for driver compilation.

Hence, its always good to use a stock kernel.

> they dropped certain
> modules including stuff which you dont really need
> in a desktop env and
> also some less popular hardware

We can't keep track of all changes that distro folks
do, hence, it is always _recommended_ that you get the
stock kernel (kernel.org), compile it and use it. 

> assuming this
> wouldnt it be simply best
> to go and compile from the stock kernel and suit it
> to our content
> when there are big differences in the kernel
> itself

You can customize it to your needs.

SK

From sundaram at redhat.com  Wed Dec 21 17:58:57 2005
From: sundaram at redhat.com (Rahul Sundaram)
Date: Wed Dec 21 17:59:11 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Hardware Compatiblity
In-Reply-To: <20051221120444.83812.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20051221120444.83812.qmail@web50213.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <43A94A89.6040404@redhat.com>

Hi

>There is no style as such. They customize it, yes.
>Sometimes, they don't even ship the sources in the
>installation CD (was it FC3 or FC4?). So, when end
>users try to build drivers, they are faced with
>problems. 
>
Not really. As mentioned in the release notes 
(http://fedora.redhat.com/docs/release-notes/fc4/#sn-kernel)  users dont 
need a source kernel to build drivers in 2.6 kernel.  Kernel drivers 
need to be in the upstream kernel and not distributed in separate 
packages ideally. Proprietary modules are one of the reasons why you 
need a external drivers which the upstream kernel does not support. In 
fact they are completely against the idea

http://lxr.linux.no/source/Documentation/stable_api_nonsense.txt

If thats really needed it is one of the repositories anyway and if you 
are looking for development. Whatever kernel headers required for module 
builders is usually in the kernel-devel package.

#yum install kernel-devel and off you go

>Ok, things are good with Ubuntu and its
>hardware detection, its an exception. 
>
More of these patches needs to be upstreamed.

>Hence, its always good to use a stock kernel.
>  
>
You basically invalidate all the QA done on a distribution kernel by 
doing it.

>We can't keep track of all changes that distro folks
>do, hence, it is always _recommended_ that you get the
>stock kernel (kernel.org), compile it and use it. 
>
>  
>
Distribution patch kernels not for fun. There are specific reasons why 
thats required at times despite best efforts. Distribution schedule is 
not in sync with kernel release schedule for example and patches pending 
upstream might be in the distribution kernel. If the vendors patch for 
feature enhancements then many of user space tools might depend on such 
patches. fbsplash or software suspend for example.

Normally end users neednt be concerned with distribution specific 
patches. If they really need to its trivial to check the repository. For 
Fedora thats http://cvs.fedora.redhat.com.

--
Rahul

From binand at gmail.com  Wed Dec 21 15:37:10 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Thu Dec 22 02:07:19 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Linux on T41
In-Reply-To: <d2a92d610512171449t1beb8614k@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d2a92d610512170803u10342292u@mail.gmail.com>
	<d2a92d610512171449t1beb8614k@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610512211237o7c6e7063l@mail.gmail.com>

I suppose an update is in order :)

The installation was a breeze - I booted into Knoppix, and used
ntfsresize to shrink the WinXP installation to 18GB - and then fdisk
to create space for Linux. This is NOT the recommended procedure for
newbies/intermediates - I personally found the interface of qtparted
clumsy, that's all :) Unless you have a complete understanding of
disks, partitions, volumes and whatnots, please do not attempt this
without parental guidance.

One difference I found in SuSE (as opposed to Redhat) is that after
installing stuff from CD1, the system reboots to the harddisk and
continues installation from there. Redhat/Fedora finishes off full
installation using as many CDs as required before rebooting to the
harddisk. I am not going to post screenshots or anything - didn't even
bother capturing any - several others have done it in far better ways.

Everything was autodetected. My e1000 network card, the CD writer (at
least, K3b shows the writer - I am yet to see if it actually manages
to write anything), sound system (haven't tested the microphone yet -
midweek here, can't fiddle around too much). The docking station could
be configured (sorry for the false alarm earlier today, folks!) using
YaST - "second monitor/keyboard/mouse". I still haven't figured out
how to blank out the LCD when I use the docking station.

Wifi has been a disappointment. First of all, it seems that
configuring WPA is a challenge (all access points I use require WPA,
except the T-Mobile hotspots which are open anyway). Secondly, I seem
to have hit upon a bug either in SuSE's packaging or ipw2100 itself -
"ipw2100-1.3.fw is not available or load failed". So I am still in
WinXP at home, typing this. A colleague pointed me here:
http://hostap.epitest.fi/wpa_supplicant/

It was far easier to configure my two important network drives - a
CIFS share and a DAV one - in Konqueror than it was in Windows.

More later. The next update should be from Linux. :)

Binand

Binand Sethumadhavan wrote:
> to have hit upon a bug either in SuSE's packaging or ipw2100 itself -
> "ipw2100-1.3.fw is not available or load failed". So I am still in
>
>   

Firmware failure may be due to two reasons. One is if there is wireless
on/off switch in laptop, that might have not enabled in linux.  second
reason is path of firmware. the path of firmware typically stored in
/etc/hotplug/firmware.agent file. your ipw2100 firmware should be
available in that part.

Regards,
T.KaruppuSwamy,

Hi Binand, Karuppuswamy, and others:

--- "T.KaruppuSwamy" <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:
> One is
> if there is wireless
> on/off switch in laptop, that might have not enabled
> in linux.

On/off switch? for in-built wireless?

> Binand Sethumadhavan wrote:
> "ipw2100-1.3.fw is not available or load failed".

Can you post the link to your current kernel .config
file. You will need to have:

  CONFIG_FW_LOADER 

set in the kernel:

Device Drivers -> Generic Driver Options -> Hotplug
firmware loading support

My assumption is that SuSE distribution kernel does
not have it enabled by default.

Just follow the instructions from here:

http://ipw2100.sourceforge.net/INSTALL

--- Karuppusamy wrote:
> second
> reason is path of firmware. the path of firmware
> typically stored in
> /etc/hotplug/firmware.agent file. your ipw2100
> firmware should be
> available in that part.

Yes.

>From the INSTALL file:

"You need to place all of these files into the hotplug
firmware directory, e.g. /usr/lib/hotplug/firmware/ 
or  /lib/firmware/.  Check the contents of the
/etc/hotplug/firmware.agent to determine the specific
location for your distribution. "

I use /usr/lib/hotplug/firmware on Debian.

Regards,

SK

From logulinux at gmx.net  Thu Dec 22 12:32:42 2005
From: logulinux at gmx.net (Logu)
Date: Thu Dec 22 12:41:26 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] dd+iso9660 how to
References: <d05619590512210615u5b7fa94fhc3867074e1468362@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <01eb01c606c6$e4c3b440$140110ac@LOGUCO>


linux:/home/student # dd if=/dev/hda6 of=cd.iso
222848+0 records in
222848+0 records out
linux:/home/student #

linux:/home/student # mount /root/cd.iso /home/student/cd -o loop
mount: you must specify the filesystem type

linux:/home/student # mount /root/cd.iso /home/student/cd -o loop -t iso9660
mount: wrong fs type, bad option, bad superblock on /dev/loop0,
or too many mounted file systems
(could this be the IDE device where you in fact use
ide-scsi so that sr0 or sda or so is needed?)
linux:/home/student #


How to instrust the dd to output a iso9660 image?
or what this means and how to use it?
------------------------------------

Actually your command will create an image of the filesystem on the disk 
partition (/dev/hda6).
In general if you dd a cdrom device you will get an iso9660. Use mkisofs to 
create iso9660 image.

-logu

solve this issue so that we can use make itself?
--------------------

The code has a makefile which is interpreted correctly by the gmake and the 
make that come with solaris interprets it differently. Go through the 
documentation of solaris make and correct them. Better install gmake instead 
of correcting the makefile for every opensource products in future.

-logu

>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>
mydestination = $myhostname, localhost, localhost.$mydomain, $mydomain, myserver.co.uk

virtual_alias_maps = hash:/etc/postfix/virtual
transport_maps = hash:/etc/postfix/transport

alias_database = hash:/etc/postfix/aliases

smtpd_recipient_restrictions = permit_mynetworks, check_sender_access hash:/etc/postfix/access, reject_unauth_destination

smtpd_sasl_security_options=noanonymous

is it a tarball or just a piece of C code ?
if it is a tarball the header file discrepency should be handled by automake
and autoconf tools provided the developer has implemented it.
if its a single C code.. then try changing the make.h to corresponding
header that solaris supports.

On 12/21/05, nava ladi <navalady@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> i have some important data on the cdrw.
> I accidently erased the data using k3b.Is there any way to get it
> now.But it is very  important now.
> Pls look all the possibilities to get it.Is the any software  or command?
> But i have not burned any data on the erased cdrw?


just put in your RW and mount it. after mounting it use dd command to create
a image of the entire disk (RW) in your hard drive. use strings to retrive
the data. but this would work if you have data in the text form.

If you did  a fast erase using k3b .. It would have deleted only the index
files. You will still have the files untouched. If you did a complete
erase.. then its difficult.

On 22/12/05, Muneer <muneerch@gmail.com> wrote:
> When I googled, I knew command gmake instead of make will resolve the
> issue. Any body know why this fails or is there any alternate way to
> solve this issue so that we can use make itself?

Your Makefile uses GNU Make extensions which are not supported on
Solaris make. Your best bet is to download GNU Make from
www.sunfreeware.com and use it to build the software.

Binand

On 12/22/05, Logu <logulinux@gmx.net> wrote:
> Hi,
>
> I was troubleshooting a linux machine and noted that they have mounted the
> whole device without partitioning it.
> ie., like "mount /dev/sdb /mnt" instead of "mount /dev/sdb1 /mnt".
>
> Is it advisable to do the above? and what are the probable issues related
> with it. I thought it was not possible to do that.

That is perfectly valid. It only means that the filesystem occupies
the entire media.
This is what happens typically for a USB stick.

Vijairaj

Hello Sud,

Kindly follow the below link. I found it very useful to use cvs. Though I 
dont use it locally but thru network.

http://www.linux.ie/articles/tutorials/cvs.php

If you are gonna add a new project then
cvs import <project name> <Ur-Comp-tag-anything> start

then cvs checkout <module-name>

then cvs add <file to be added>

//Now it will be scheduled

then its cvs commit !!

Everything goes on cvs repositry :).

Also Eclipse IDE has got good binding with CVS I guess.. May be u can try 
it..

Cheers,
Aanjhan

Hi,

 I have a c code which successfully compiles on RedHat platform (gcc
and 32 bit processor). The same code I tried to compile on Solaris
platform (64 bit SPARC).
It throughs the following warning.

 warning: cast increases required alignment of target type

The code is some thing like this:
struct y{
signed int a1;
....
...
};
struct x {
struct y *header
unsigned char * data
};
unsigned short * Buf
struct x * packet;

packet=(struct x *)malloc (sizeof(struct x));
Buf = (unsigned short *) packet->header;

Last line results in warning. struct x and struct y has bigger size
than unsigned short.

Can any body tell me why this warning is coming?

Thanks and Regards
Muneer CH

From binand at gmail.com  Sat Dec 24 04:43:54 2005
From: binand at gmail.com (Binand Sethumadhavan)
Date: Sat Dec 24 15:14:05 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Compilation warning in Solaris
In-Reply-To: <72a9b0620512240124n1c650ed7oe6ba6a7639f6ac9d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <72a9b0620512240124n1c650ed7oe6ba6a7639f6ac9d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d2a92d610512240143w30afee3bt@mail.gmail.com>

On 24/12/05, Muneer <muneerch@gmail.com> wrote:
> unsigned short * Buf
> struct x * packet;
>
> packet=(struct x *)malloc (sizeof(struct x));
> Buf = (unsigned short *) packet->header;
>
> Last line results in warning. struct x and struct y has bigger size
> than unsigned short.

It should throw a warning on Redhat too. Try compiling with gcc -Wall.

> Can any body tell me why this warning is coming?

It is obvious, isn't it? You have pointed it out yourself. Your Buf
needs to be a struct y * or void * - I really don't know why you have
chosen unsigned short *.

Secondly, it is bad programming practice to cast the return value from
malloc(). Drop it.

Thirdly, the way you have presented your code, you know that it will
coredump if you try to dereference Buf, right?

Binand

ubuntu 10.4 :o... you either mean 5.04 or 5.10!!!

> the repository,
> when i added them to source.list file,
> and made
> sudo apt-get update

my sources.list file for breezy (5.10):
## Uncomment the following two lines to fetch updated software from the
network
deb http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy main restricted
deb-src http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy main restricted

## Uncomment the following two lines to fetch major bug fix updates
produced
## after the final release of the distribution.
deb http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy-updates main restricted
deb-src http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy-updates main restricted

## Uncomment the following two lines to add software from the 'universe'
## repository.
## N.B. software from this repository is ENTIRELY UNSUPPORTED by the
Ubuntu
## team, and may not be under a free licence. Please satisfy yourself as
to
## your rights to use the software. Also, please note that software in
## universe WILL NOT receive any review or updates from the Ubuntu
security
## team.
deb http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy universe
deb-src http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy universe

deb http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy-security main restricted
deb-src http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy-security main
restricted

deb http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy-security universe
deb-src http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy-security universe

deb http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy multiverse
deb-src http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy multiverse

## Ubuntu Backports
deb http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu breezy-backports main universe
multiverse restricted

deb http://in.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/ breezy main restricted
deb-src http://in.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/ breezy main restricted

Yesterday , i installed OpenSuse Desktop at my work place. I wonder
how it went well without any problem. Since i did Internet
installation, i was surprised to see. Simple installation screen, Good
GUI, more professional etc. I just downloaded internet installation
iso image and invoked that from GRUB and started with installation. at
first, it gives me CUI. somewhat i managed and succeeeded in
installing after whole day downloading more than G's. Atlast i was
asked to give instructions to the installaer and it succeeded the
installation. The Bootloader is good at GUI. When i went into the
login screen, i was surprised to see something like Windows XP Login
screen, Pleasant Color Combination, eye catching and to say simple
"it's sexy". I liked it very much. YAST Tool is good for newbies. I
can suggest for newbies that they should try OpenSuse 10 and try to
feel the power of Openness.

OpenSuse the Great :)

Subject: [Ilugc] [OT]previewseek.com - discussion

On 27/12/05, T.KaruppuSwamy <swamytk@tandbintl.com> wrote:
> Any body has tried search engine beta.previewseek.com ? It seems to be
> good. your opinion?

First impression: Notwithstanding all the claims they have in their
About Us page, I think it is just a front-end to a lot of web
services. Taking their own example query, Java, I get a page that
says:

The term Java can refer to:

In geography:
[snip]
# In computer science:
[snip]
# Java may also mean:
[snip]

Which looks suspiciously identical to: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Java

Then, looking at the search result, the "archived" link is to the
wayback machine. Rest of it is all just what is in Google ("Similar
Pages" => "Find more like this", "More results from www.fubar.com" =>
"more from this site").

They do a bit of Google bashing, of course. When they say: "On Google,
if you were interested in Java the island, you would have to click
through over 70 pages of irrelevant results for 'java' before getting
to your very first relevant result", they really lack a clue - the
first result on Google for "java island" is the 100% relevant
Wikipedia entry for the island.

Among the other claims they have:

"It visits all the major search engines on your behalf" - does this
mean that the actual search is done by Google and the like? A9 or
Metacrawler, anyone?

Binand

From sens2003 at gmail.com  Wed Dec 28 06:14:21 2005
From: sens2003 at gmail.com (Senthil)
Date: Wed Dec 28 06:14:29 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] foreign keys in mysql
In-Reply-To: <d59d94320512260459n742b375flcccfdc0f60ab26fb@mail.gmail.com>
References: <d59d94320512260459n742b375flcccfdc0f60ab26fb@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <14c320c90512271644n60b4718ex4740769a2f09be8b@mail.gmail.com>

> i tried creating foreign key in mysql,but i was not able to create it.
> the query i used was..
>
>       "create table parent(id int not null, primary key(id))type=innodb;"
>
>       "create table child (childid int, index(childid),foriegn key(childid)
> references parent(id))type=innodb;"
>
> It keeps inserting values not in parent table.
> Is this the way to create foreign key in mysql.
> Are there any configuration details to be modified.

the innodb feature may not be enabled by default.
to enable the innodb feature remove the "skip-innodb"
line from the mysql configuration file my.cnf and try adding
the following lines then restart the mysql server.

# location where mysql database is stored
innodb_data_home_dir = /var/lib/mysql/
innodb_data_file_path = ibdata1:10M:autoextend
innodb_log_group_home_dir = /var/lib/mysql/
innodb_log_arch_dir = /var/lib/mysql/

# You can set .._buffer_pool_size up to 50 - 80 %
# of RAM but beware of setting memory usage too high
innodb_buffer_pool_size = 16M
innodb_additional_mem_pool_size = 2M

# Set .._log_file_size to 25 % of buffer pool size
innodb_log_file_size = 5M
innodb_log_buffer_size = 8M
innodb_flush_log_at_trx_commit = 1
innodb_lock_wait_timeout = 50


These details could be found in the sample configuration file.
In debian i found these details in
/usr/share/doc/mysql-server/examples/my-small.cnf file.

---
S.Senthil Kumaran
http://sskganesan.blogspot.com

Hello, I did reply to you yesterday.

Anyways, if you have installed from source (assuming MySQL user/group is
mysqluser, otherwise don't pass the --user argument), you can start MySQL
using:

shell> sudo /path/to/mysqld_safe --user=mysqluser &

or, if you did a binary installation, you can start MySQL using:

shell> sudo /etc/init.d/mysql start
(at least on SUSE).

The MySQL team has taken pains to write an excellent documentation, please take
some time to read it:

  http://dev.mysql.com/doc/refman/5.0/en/

Gopalarathnam Venkatesan
http://gopalarathnam.com/

Subject: [Ilugc] [slightly OT] 64 vs 32 bit processors
In-Reply-To: <20051231002648.GA29449@mrna.tn.nic.in>
References: <20051230193703.GA28279@mrna.tn.nic.in>
	<32b5ee760512280829n1f7a3e81w22b7aed9ba5cbea@mail.gmail.com>
	<20051231002648.GA29449@mrna.tn.nic.in>
Message-ID: <5d0d0e310512281032l26bab78cmd9e2eadfdaa6b95b@mail.gmail.com>

On 12/31/05, km <km@mrna.tn.nic.in> wrote:

> 'AMD Opteron' specs say that 32 & 64 bit programs can simultaneously coexist, allowing for a smooth transition to 64 bit architecture while considering overall deployment costs, but in practice i dont know the bottlenecks. any ideas over this?

I have an Athlon 64 that had 64 bit Ubuntu running on it for some time. Most
applications and the kernel itself were 64 bit. For applications like
flash, java and
OO, which don't have 64 bit versions yet I used a chrooted environment
with the 32
bit libraries. One day when I wanted to update to the latest version
of the distro, I
found it was too much a time to waste on a home system maintaining two sets of
libraries, so I am currently running only the 32 bit version and quite happy.

I am planning to follow this stratergy untill the time when 64 bit
processors will
become more common and have their due respect.

Fedora, if i am right follows a different architecture and don't need
a chroot, the
libraries have different naming convention and can happily exist side-by-side.

The moral of the story is, Check if all the applications you need have a 64 bit
version and that you are picking the right distro.

--
Vijairaj

*Job Title: Engineer ? Community Relations* *Job Responsibilities*

   - Author fixes, execute builds, run tests, resolve test failures  and
   write Regression Tests
   - Promote a high level of customer satisfaction by providing thorough
   and useful information, cultivating good working relationships with
   Developer Relation Engineers (DREs), Engineering Team, Customers, Open
   Source Community
   - Build outstanding relations with and contribute to Open Source
   community projects
   - Clearly articulate to customers and management a problem definition
   and resolution plan.
   - Work with Engineering and Product Management to contribute to
   product quality, product enhancements, and product design decisions.
   - Foster teamwork in solving customer, process and organizational
   issues.  Handle multiple issues simultaneously and adapt to shifting
   priorities
   - Follow-through and complete tasks independently.  Participate in
   team-based activities and group projects
   - Write knowledge articles based on issues encountered by customers or
   issues that you have researched and believe that customers will encounter
   - Participate in the open source community by reading and posting
   mailing lists/discussion forums, providing bug fixes,
   suggesting/contributing feature enhancement requests etc.

*Qualifications & Experience *

   - BE/ B-Tech or BS in Computer Science or equivalent
   - 4+ years of work experience in sustaining engineering, professional
   services and/or software development with related technologies.  With
   Minimum 3+ years of experience in developing applications using  *two
   or more* of the following middleware stacks:
      - Apache + J2EE application server + MySQL/PostgreSQL
      - Apache + Tomcat or other servlet container + MySQL/PostgreSQL
      - Apache + PHP + MySQL/PostgreSQL
      - Apache + Perl | Python + MySQL/PostgreSQL
   - Experience with open source RDBMS such as MySQL and PostgreSQL
   - Solid understanding of enterprise software development methodology,
   accompanying infrastructure and process.  Knowledge of operating system
   flags and utilities for Windows and Linux platforms.
   - 3+ years experience with two or more of the following languages/
   language frameworks


   C, C++, PHP, Java ? J2SE, J2EE, Perl, Python

*Desirable*

   - Ability to work independently with minimal management direction.
   - Passion for working with people, and a strong interest in helping
   customers succeed.
   - Passion for open source and a strong interest in contributing to the
   open source community.
   - Very strong written and verbal communication skills, with an ability
   to speak confidently and communicate effectively (in-person, by phone, or by
   email) with customers, other developers within and outside SpikeSource, and
   senior management.
   - Ability to troubleshoot customer issues, research related
   information in appropriate open source communities, coordinate issue
   reporting/resolution with other developers within and outside SpikeSource,
   and test fixes.
   - Ability to maintain and document customer communication.
   - Ability to contribute to internal knowledge by updating/adding
   knowledge articles.
   - Ability to lead or participate in team projects that enhance quality
   and efficiency of SpikeSource's support.
   - Ability to learn new technologies quickly.
   - Ability to multitask effectively and work well under pressure

Subject: [Ilugc] CD-ROM mount problem
In-Reply-To: <BAY7-F148E599FEA04E38034C0B2CC360@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <20051229162016.47064.qmail@web51906.mail.yahoo.com>


> try ( #automount 
> /dev/cdrom /mnt/cdrom ) command bcz this will create
> a auto mount point. 
> also say # service autofs start. it will show an

I don't have the commands 'service' or 'automount'.
Do they come with debian?

> insert a 
> cd from normal user account. then c. otherwise send
> me deatail description 

This is in my fstab:

bigblackbox:~# cat /etc/fstab | grep cdrom
/dev/cdrom      /media/cdrom0   iso9660 ro,user,noauto
 0       0

Though it is noauto, the cdrom is mounted
automatically(!)
when I insert a cd into the drive. I am able to browse
/media/cdrom0
through nautilus.
The entry in /etc/mtab also confirms this:

bigblackbox:~# cat /etc/mtab | grep cdrom
/dev/cdrom /media/cdrom0 iso9660
ro,nosuid,nodev,noexec 0 0

Though the CD has mounted, the icon that should come
on the gnome desktop
does not appear.

Also when I try to umount the cdrom there is an error:
bigblackbox:~# umount /dev/cdrom
umount: /dev/cdrom: not mounted

This is quite contrary to what /etc/mtab says.

When I try to umount using the following command there
is an error
(see below):
bigblackbox:~# umount /media/cdrom0
umount: /media/cdrom0: device is busy
umount: /media/cdrom0: device is busy

To find which process is keeping the CD busy, I did
this:
bigblackbox:~# find /proc -lname "*cdrom*" 2>/dev/null
/proc/2779/task/2779/fd/95

bigblackbox:~# ls -al /proc/2779/task/2779/fd/95
lr-x------  1 root root 64 2005-12-29 21:38
/proc/2779/task/2779/fd/95 -> /media/cdrom0

bigblackbox:~# ps -ef | grep 2779
ram       2779     1  0 21:14 ?        00:00:00
/usr/sbin/famd -T 0

So I guess that famd is doing the mount and blocking
the umount.
All this didn't happen until the CD-ROM drive changed
from hdc to hdd.

Any suggestions on how to solve this?

Thanks & Regards,
Ram

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Fri Dec 30 07:52:53 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Fri Dec 30 07:46:08 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: IPR in Computer software
In-Reply-To: <34602.59.94.112.28.1135795351.squirrel@mail.allahabadhighcourt.in>
References: <34602.59.94.112.28.1135795351.squirrel@mail.allahabadhighcourt.in>
Message-ID: <43B499FD.8020004@gmail.com>

bbls_ps@allahabadhighcourt.in wrote:

>Dear Sir
>The aforesaid article and some other articles by his lordship Justice
>Yatindra Singh dealing with computer software, open source are available
>on the web site of the Allahabad high court (www.allahabadhighcourt.in).
>They may be seen by going to the
>web Diary - Item Wise - speech/article or may be accessed at
>http://www.allahabadhighcourt.in/calendar/itemWiseList.jsp?group=11
>
>Yours truly
>BBL Srivastava
>
Thank you for the information.  I'll forward the news to other mailing 
lists that would find the articles and site interesting and useful too.  
It is heartening to know that the Allahabad High Court is using free and 
open software and standards so extensively. If I may say so, the 
articles by Hon'ble Mr. Justice Yatindra Singh have approached free 
software from a neutral point of view and present a fair picture to the 
reader. 

In the talk titled "OPEN SOURCE SOFTWARE AND INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY 
RIGHTS" delivered by Justice Yatindra Singh at NALSAR Hyderabad and NLS, 
Bangalore and NUJS, Kolkata, Linus Torvalds has been quoted from "Just 
for Fun: the Story of an Accidental Revolutionary' as
saying:

"The GPL and open source model allows for the creation of the best 
technology.
... It also prevents the hoarding of technology and ensures that anyone with
interest won't be excluded from its development.

So open source would rather use the legal weapon of copyright as an 
invitation
to join in the fun, rather than as a weapon against others. It's still 
the same old
mantra: Make Love, Not War, except on a slightly more abstract level."

The quote captures the key IPR feature central to free software, and 
makes the legal intricacies involved superfluous.
The practical reasons why many prefer to use free software is succintly 
summarised in the following words:

"I shifted to GPLed software few years ago: the reasons were practicable.
GPLed software comes without any cost. And it does what I do--word 
processing,
playing music, watching Video, surfing internet,and electronically 
managing my
calendar --as well as any other proprietary software."

More generally, the observations on using computers in the talk titled 
"IT: The Road to Speedier Justice" is remarkable:

"Computers are like 'English butlers'.  They have to be told what to do 
and they do it in that way and no other way. Computers love routine and 
are never bored. But to achieve any success the minds of the judges, 
lawyers, and court employees have to be streamlined into a method. One 
has to leave individualism. The reports cannot be generated unless data 
is fed into computers; they will not have any meaning unless they are 
utilised and goals are fixed. And above all, if there is no will to 
change, no orientation to the work culture, then nothing can work."

Sacrificing individuality is a small price to pay for the larger 
benefits received in return by the general public.  Probably NRC-FOSS ( 
http://www.au-kbc.org/nrcf/index.htm )could include some of the articles 
as part of the curriculum for students.  Public institutions that have 
not yet adopted free software practices need to wake up now.

Thanks,
Ramanraj K
__
References:
http://www.allahabadhighcourt.in/event/OSS_&_IPR.pdf
http://www.allahabadhighcourt.in/event/IT_-_Speedier_Justice.pdf
http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/pipermail/ilugc/2005-November/022135.html (My 
previous post to ilugc about the article titled "Intellectual Property 
Rights in Computer Software" by Justice Yatindra Singh of the Allahabad 
High Court published in AIR 2005 Journal 353.

On Friday 30 Dec 2005 10:36 am, indu veni wrote:
> I am doing php coding and in that for uploading a file
> and downloading it I have error. Can any one guide me
> in coding this.

this is not a php problem - it is just html, you need to create a 
form like so:

<form enctype="multipart/form-data", method="post" 
action="somescript>
<input type="file" name="file_to_upload"/>
</form>

and then process the POST data
